or any group or combination acting as a unit, and includes the plural as well
as the singular, unless the intent to give to a more limited meaning is
disclosed by the context in which it is used.
RETAIL WINE LICENSE: A license issued by the director of the Idaho state police
authorizing a person to sell table wine and/or dessert wine at retail for
consumption off the licensed premises.
RETAILER: A person to whom a retail wine license has been issued.
WINE: Includes table wine and dessert wine, unless the context requires
otherwise. (1996 Code § 2-5-1; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2C-2: LICENSE REQUIRED; APPLICATION:
   A.   License Required: It shall be lawful for any person to sell wine at
retail within the corporate limits of the city after having first procured a
license therefor. (1996 Code § 2-5-2)
   B.   Application For License: Application for license shall be in writing,
signed and sworn to by the applicant upon application forms furnished by the
clerk-treasurer. Such application shall be filed by the clerk-treasurer, along
with proof of equivalent state and county licenses, and presented to the mayor
and council at a meeting of the city council for their approval, rejection or
further consideration. (1996 Code § 2-5-3)
3-2C-3: QUALIFICATIONS FOR LICENSE:
The applicant for license shall possess all of the qualifications necessary to
obtain a license from the director of the Idaho state police, and maintain such
qualifications throughout the period for which such license is issued. The
possession of licenses regularly issued by the said state department and the
county, in addition to a city beer license, shall be prima facie evidence of
the applicant's qualifications to receive a license hereunder. (1996 Code § 2-
5-4; amd. 2010 Code)
3-2C-4: LICENSE FEE; TERM:
The license fee imposed and collected shall be the sum of one hundred dollars
($100.00) per year. Such license year shall be from one minute past twelve
o'clock (12:01) A.M. January 1 through December 31. Such fee shall be imposed
and collected for all or any portion of the year. (1996 Code § 2-5-5)
3-2C-5: ISSUANCE OF LICENSE:
Upon filing the application for a license and production of evidence, as
required by section
3-2C-3 of this article, as to the qualification of the applicant and by payment
of the required license fee, the clerk-treasurer shall, upon approval of the
city council, issue to the applicant a license to sell wine at retail within
the city for such calendar year or the remainder thereof. (1996 Code § 2-5-6)
3-2C-6: TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
The assignment or transfer of a wine license shall be the same as provided by
city ordinance providing for the assignment or transfer of a beer license as
provided in section
3-2B-6 of this chapter. (1996 Code § 2-5-7)
3-2C-7: CONSUMPTION ON PREMISES:
Retailers who do not possess a valid license for the retail sale of liquor by
the drink shall not permit consumption of wine on the licensed premises and may
sell the wine only in its original unbroken, sealed container. Wine sold for
consumption on the retailer's premises may be sold only during hours that
liquor by the drink may be sold pursuant to the laws of the state. Wine sold by
the retailer for consumption off the premises of the retailer may be sold only
during the hours that beer may be sold pursuant to the laws of the state. (1996
Code § 2-5-8)
3-2C-8: POSSESSION; TRANSPORTATION OF OPEN CONTAINER:
No person may, while operating in or upon a motor vehicle upon a public street
of the city, have in his possession any wine in an open or unsealed container
of any kind. (1996 Code § 2-5-9)
3-2C-9: RESTRICTIONS CONCERNING MINORS:
   A.   Consumption Or Possession:
      1.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years may consume or
possess wine.
      2.   No person shall give, sell or deliver wine to any person under the
age of twenty one (21) years.
   B.   Misrepresentation Of Age:
      1.   No person under the age of twenty one (21) years shall, by any
means, represent to any retailer or distributor or to any agent or employee of
such retailer or distributor that he is twenty one (21) years or more of age
for the purpose of inducing such retailer or distributor, or his agent or
employee, to sell, serve or dispense wine to such person.
      2.   No person shall, by any means, represent to any retailer or
distributor, or the agent or employee of such retailer or distributor, that any
other person is twenty one (21) years or more of age, when in fact such other
person is under the age of twenty one (21) years, for the purpose of inducing
such retailer or distributor to sell, serve or dispense wine to such other
person. (1996 Code § 2-5-10)
3-2C-10: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The right shall be and remain at all times vested in the mayor and city
council, and the mayor and city council may, as hereinafter provided, revoke or
cancel any license for fraud or misrepresentation in its procurement, or for
violation of any of the provisions of this article, or for any conduct or act
of the licensee or his employees, or any conduct or act permitted by him or
them on the premises where such business is conducted, or in connection
therewith, or adjacent thereto, tending to render such business or such
premises where the same is conducted as a public nuisance or a menace to the
health, peace, safety or general welfare of the city; provided, that revocation
or suspension of the state license by the director of the Idaho state police
shall be deemed prima facie evidence for revocation or suspension of the
license issued herein. (1996 Code § 2-5-11; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 3
AMUSEMENTS AND SPECIAL EVENTS
SECTION:
3-3-1: License And Insurance Required
3-3-2: Mechanical Rides, Location
3-3-3: Circuses And Carnivals
3-3-4: License Fees For Rides
3-3-5: Concessionaires And Special Affairs Producers
3-3-1: LICENSE AND INSURANCE REQUIRED:
   A.   License Required; Posting: It shall be unlawful for any person to
operate, engage in or carry on any business, amusement or device as referred to
in this chapter without first obtaining a city license therefor. Such license
shall be posted on the site during the operation of such. (1996 Code §
2-1-1)
   B.   Insurance Required: Before a license shall be issued, proof of
insurance shall be shown, naming the city as an additional insured. Such
insurance shall be no less than one hundred thousand dollars ($100,000.00) per
occurrence. (1996 Code §
2-1-4; amd. 2010 Code)
3-3-2: MECHANICAL RIDES, LOCATION:
Any person who shall make application to the clerk-treasurer for a license to
conduct or operate any merry-go-round or mechanical device giving rides to
people shall, at the same time of making such application, file with the clerk-
treasurer a written statement, particularly describing the location of the
place where the person desires to conduct or operate such mechanical rides.
(1996 Code §
2-1-2)
3-3-3: CIRCUSES AND CARNIVALS:
   A.   Deposit Required: Before a license shall be issued to a manager, owner
or operator of a circus, menagerie or carnival, if such activity is to take
place inside the city park, such person shall be required to deposit with the
clerk-treasurer a cash deposit of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00), such
deposit to be a guarantee that after the period during which the circus,
menagerie or carnival is operated, the grounds used for each operation shall be
cleaned of all trash, paper and other debris caused to be deposited thereon by
said circus, menagerie or carnival. (1996 Code §
2-1-3; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Cleanup; Refund Of Deposit: Before returning said deposit to the
depositor, the clerk-treasurer shall have such grounds, street or streets
inspected for the purpose of ascertaining that such cleaning has been done.
(1996 Code §
2-1-3)
3-3-4: LICENSE FEES FOR RIDES:
There shall be a minimum license fee for up to and including four (4) rides,
with an additional charge per ride over the initial four (4). Said license
fees, to be set by resolution by the city council, shall be paid to the city
clerk- treasurer prior to operation of a circus, menagerie or carnival. (1996
Code §
2-1-5)
3-3-5: CONCESSIONAIRES AND SPECIAL AFFAIRS PRODUCERS:
   A.   Concessionaires:
      1.   Deposit Required: Before a license shall be issued to any person to
operate a concession in the limits of the city, any such applicant shall be
required to deposit with the clerk- treasurer a sum as set by resolution to
guarantee that, after the period the special affair is operated, the grounds
shall be cleared of all trash, paper and other debris.
      2.   Cleanup; Refund Of Deposit: The clerk-treasurer shall cause the
premises to be inspected and if the clerk-treasurer finds the same to be
cleared and cleaned of such trash and debris, shall refund the deposit to such
applicant, otherwise said deposit shall be and remain the property of the city.
   B.   Special Affairs Producers:
      1.   Deposit Required: Before a license shall be issued to any person to
conduct or produce any fundraising special affairs on the public parks of the
city, any such applicant shall be required to deposit with the clerk-treasurer
a sum as set by resolution to serve as a user fee and to guarantee that, after
the period the special affair is operated, the grounds will be cleared of all
trash, paper and other debris.
      2.   Waiver: Such fee cannot be waived except by special request to the
city council from youth oriented, not for profit groups.
      3.   Cleanup; Refund Of Deposit: The clerk-treasurer shall cause the
premises to be inspected and if the clerk-treasurer finds the same to be
cleared and cleaned of such trash and debris, shall refund the deposit to such
applicant, otherwise said deposit shall be and remain the property of the city.
(1996 Code §
2-1-6; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 4
POOL, BILLIARD HALLS AND CARD ROOMS
SECTION:
3-4-1: Licenses Required; Fees
3-4-2: Minors Restricted
3-4-1: LICENSES REQUIRED; FEES:
   A.   Licenses Required:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate, maintain or conduct
a billiard, pool or bagatelle or pigeonhole table open to the public without
having first obtained a license therefor as is herein required.
      2.   All applications for such licenses shall state thereon the intended
location of the place of business and the number of tables to be used therein.
(1996 Code § 2-2-1)
   B.   Fees; License Nontransferable:
      1.   Before a license shall be issued to any person to operate or open a
billiard or pool hall or card room, said person shall pay to the clerk-
treasurer a license fee. Fees shall be set by resolution of the city council on
an annual basis. Such license shall expire on the last day of each year.
      2.   The license under this chapter shall be nontransferable. (1996 Code
§ 2-2-2)
3-4-2: MINORS RESTRICTED:
Minors under the age of eighteen (18) years shall, under no circumstances,
frequent, loiter, go or remain in any hall licensed hereunder at any time if
alcohol is on the premises, unless it be upon some lawful errand and sent under
the direction and the consent and knowledge of the parent, guardian or other
person having custody of such minor, and it shall be unlawful for the
proprietor of any hall so licensed to allow or permit any such minor to
frequent, loiter or remain within the hall in violation of this section. (1996
Code § 2-2-3)
CHAPTER 5
PEDDLERS AND ITINERANT MERCHANTS
SECTION:
3-5-1: Definition
3-5-2: License Required; Term; Fee
3-5-3: Application For License
3-5-4: Exhibition Of License
3-5-5: License Nontransferable
3-5-6: Loud Noises And Loudspeakers
3-5-7: Uninvited Peddlers Declared Nuisance
3-5-8: Revocation Of License
3-5-1: DEFINITION:
   A.   For the purpose of this chapter, a "transient merchant", "itinerant
merchant", or "itinerant vendor" is defined as any person, whether as owner,
agent, consignee or employee, whether a resident of the city or not, who
engages in a temporary business of selling and delivering goods, wares and
merchandise within the city; and who, in furtherance of such purpose, hires,
leases, uses or occupies any building, structure, motor vehicle, tent, railroad
boxcar or boat, public room in hotels, lodging houses, apartments, shops or any
place within the city, for the exhibition and sale of such goods, wares and
merchandise, either privately or at public auction.
   B.   The person so engaged shall not be relieved from complying with the
provisions of this chapter merely by reason of associating temporarily with any
local dealer, trader, merchant or auctioneer, or by conducting such transient
business in connection with, as a part of, or in the name of any local dealer,
trader, merchant or auctioneer.
   C.   This definition shall not include any nonprofit or public organization
as determined by the state. (1996 Code § 2-6-1)
3-5-2: LICENSE REQUIRED; TERM; FEE:
   A.   License Required; Term: It shall be unlawful for a transient merchant,
itinerant merchant, or itinerant vendor to engage in such business within the
city without first obtaining a license therefor in compliance with the
provisions of this chapter, and all such licenses issued under the provisions
hereof shall expire ninety (90) days after the date of issuance thereof unless
a prior date is fixed therein. (1996 Code § 2-6-2)
   B.   License Fee: Licensees under this chapter shall pay a fee as set by
resolution. (1996 Code § 2-6-3; amd. 2010 Code)
3-5-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Applicants for a license under this chapter, whether a person, firm or
corporation, shall file a written sworn application signed by the applicant if
an individual, by all partners if a partnership and by the president if a
corporation, with the clerk-treasurer, showing:
   A.   The name of the person having the management or supervision of the
applicant's business during the time that it is proposed that it will be
carried on in the city; the local address of such person while engaged in such
business; the permanent address of such person; the capacity in which such
person will act (that is, whether as proprietor, agent or otherwise); the name
and address of the person for whose account the business will be carried on, if
any; and if a corporation, under the laws of the state the same is
incorporated.
   B.   The place in the city where it is proposed to carry on the applicant's
business, and the length of time during which it is proposed that said business
shall be conducted.
   C.   A statement of the nature, character and quality of the goods, wares or
merchandise to be sold or offered for sale by the applicant in the city.
   D.   Credentials from the person for whom the applicant proposed to do
business, authorizing the applicant to act as such representative.
   E.   Such other reasonable information as to the identity or character of
the person having the management or supervision of the applicant's business or
the method or plan of doing such business as the clerk-treasurer may deem
proper to fulfill the purpose of this chapter in the protection of the public
good. (1996 Code § 2-6-4)
3-5-4: EXHIBITION OF LICENSE:
The license issued under this chapter shall be posted conspicuously in the
place of business named therein. In the event that such person applying for
said license shall desire to do business in more than one place within the
city, separate licenses shall be issued for each place of business, and shall
be posted conspicuously in each place of business. (1996 Code § 2-6-5)
3-5-5: LICENSE NONTRANSFERABLE:
No license shall be transferred. (1996 Code § 2-6-6)
3-5-6: LOUD NOISES AND LOUDSPEAKERS:
No licensee under this chapter, nor anyone in his behalf, shall shout, make an
outcry, blow a horn, ring a bell or use any other sound device, including any
loudspeaking radio or amplifying system upon any of the streets, alleys, parks
or other public places or upon any private premises in the city where sound of
sufficient volume is emitted or produced therefrom capable of being plainly
heard upon the streets, avenues, alleys or parks or other public places for the
purpose of attracting attention to any goods, wares or merchandise which such
licensee proposes to sell. (1996 Code § 2-6-7)
3-5-7: UNINVITED PEDDLERS DECLARED NUISANCE:
   A.   Nuisance Declared: The practice of going in and upon private residences
in the city by solicitors, peddlers, hawkers, itinerant merchants or transient
vendors of merchandise not having been requested or invited so to do by the
owner or occupant of said residences for the purpose of soliciting orders for
the sale of goods, wares and merchandise and/or disposing of and/or peddling or
hawking the same is declared to be a nuisance and punishable as such nuisance
as a misdemeanor.
   B.   Posting Of Sign: Any property posting a sign restricting peddlers shall
constitute a withdrawal of permission or invitation. (1996 Code § 2-6-8)
3-5-8: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
   A.   Causes For Revocation: The licenses issued pursuant to this chapter may
be revoked by the city council, after notice and hearing, for any of the
following causes:
      1.   Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement contained in the
application for license.
      2.   Any fraud, misrepresentation or false statement made in connection
with the selling of goods, wares or merchandise.
      3.   Any violation of this chapter.
      4.   Conducting the business licensed under this chapter in an unlawful
manner or in such a manner as to constitute a breach of the peace or to
constitute a menace to the health, safety or general welfare of the public.
   B.   Notice Of Hearing: Notice of hearing for revocation of a license shall
be given, in writing, setting forth specifically the grounds of the complaint
and the time and place of the hearing. (1996 Code § 2-6-9)
CHAPTER 6
AUTOMOBILE WRECKING YARDS
SECTION:
3-6-1: Definition
3-6-2: Operation Or Expansion Prohibited
3-6-3: Penalty
3-6-1: DEFINITION:
An "automobile wrecking yard" is defined as a place of business where one or
more unserviceable, discarded, worn out, or junked automobiles or bodies,
engines, tires, parts, or accessories are gathered together and stored. (1996
Code §
7-2-2)
3-6-2: OPERATION OR EXPANSION PROHIBITED:
   A.   Operation: It is in the best interest of the public health, safety and
welfare of the inhabitants of the city that the operation of automobile
wrecking yards be prohibited and controlled within the city limits. (1996 Code
§
7-2-1)
   B.   Establishment Or Commencement: From and after the effective date
hereof, it shall be unlawful to establish or commence the operation of an
automobile wrecking yard within the city limits. (1996 Code §
7-2-3)
   C.   Expansion: From and after the effective date hereof, it shall be
unlawful for any existing automobile wrecking yard to expand or enlarge its
area of operation. (1996 Code §
7-2-4)
3-6-3: PENALTY:
A violation of this chapter shall be and constitute a misdemeanor and shall be
punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1996 Code §
7-2-5)
TITLE 4
HEALTH, SANITATION AND ENVIRONMENT
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
4-1-1: Definition
4-1-2: Offensive Deposits; Obstructions On Public Ways
4-1-3: Noises
4-1-4: Noxious Weeds
4-1-5: Offensive Premises; Cleanup
4-1-6: Keeping Junk
4-1-7: Dead Animals
4-1-8: Charges For Abatement Of Weeds And Other Nuisances
4-1-1: DEFINITION:
Anything which is injurious to health or which is indecent or offensive to the
senses, or an obstruction to the free passage or use in the customary manner of
any street, alley, sidewalk, or public park, or injures any street, alley or
public park, or disturbs the peace and quiet is hereby declared to be a
"nuisance". (1996 Code §
7-1-1)
4-1-2: OFFENSIVE DEPOSITS; OBSTRUCTIONS ON PUBLIC WAYS:
   A.   Rubbish Deposits: Any person who shall wilfully or negligently throw,
dump, store or deposit upon any sidewalk, street, alley or public place, or any
portion thereof, any glass, nails, tacks, hoops, cans, barbed wire, boards, or
any other substance or material which would be likely to injure any horse,
stock, vehicle or person traveling thereon, or which obstructs or impedes the
free passage of pedestrians or public travel upon such sidewalk, street, alley
or public place or any portion thereof, shall be deemed in violation of this
chapter.
   B.   Water Flowing Or Fires On Public Ways: It shall be unlawful for any
person to:
      1.   Wilfully or negligently allow irrigation water to flow upon the
street in such a manner that it stands in pools or continuously flows upon said
streets.
      2.   Allow overflow water from air conditioners to run across or stand
upon the sidewalks or streets.
      3.   Burn leaves, grass or other materials upon the streets.
   C.   Obstructing Sidewalks: It shall be unlawful for any person to place any
display, sign, merchandise or other obstruction upon any public sidewalk. (1996
Code §
7-1-2)
4-1-3: NOISES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a radio, television set,
loudspeaking or other noisome device in such a manner that it disturbs the
peace and quiet of nearby residents. (1996 Code §
7-1-4; amd. 2010 Code)
4-1-4: NOXIOUS WEEDS:
   A.   Nuisance Declared; Cutting Or Removal Required: All offensive and
noxious weeds or plants are hereby declared to be a public nuisance and shall
be cut, removed and destroyed by the owner or agent of the ground or premises
on which the same are located, when notified to do so by the mayor or the city
council. (1996 Code §
7-1-3; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Failure To Remove Weeds; Violation: Any person owning or controlling
any such property upon whom notice has been served to remove said noxious
weeds, who fails to comply with said notice within the time specified in said
notice shall be violating the provisions of this code. (1996 Code §
7-1-3)
4-1-5: OFFENSIVE PREMISES; CLEANUP:
   A.   Refuse, Stagnant Water; Cleanup:
      1.   No person shall permit or suffer to be in or accommodate in or upon
any yard, lot, place or premises or upon any street or sidewalk adjacent to or
abutting upon any lot, block, place, premises or in any building or shed owned
or occupied by said person or for which he may be the agent within the limits
of the city any stagnant or impure water, refuse, vegetable decay or decaying
substance, garbage or filth of any kind, nor suffer such yard, lot, place,
building or premises to be or to remain in such condition as to cause or create
a nuisance or offensive smell or to pollute or render unhealthful the
atmosphere or premises or thereby to be, become, cause or create a public
nuisance. (1996 Code §
7-1-5)
      2.   Any person violating this provision shall clean up said premises and
abate such nuisance within forty eight (48) hours after having received notice
of said condition from the city council. (1996 Code §
7-1-5; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Offensive Matter: It shall be unlawful for any person to place upon
property, or to allow to remain upon any property within said person's control,
any matter which is offensive to the senses or injurious to health as
determined by the city council. (1996 Code §
7-1-5)
4-1-6: KEEPING JUNK:
   A.   Definition: "Junk" is hereby defined to be any used material or any
parts of material units which have become useless for the purpose for which
said material was originally fabricated or manufactured and shall include, but
not be limited to, automobiles not licensed for the current year and any
unsightly accumulation of garbage, rubbish or debris.
   B.   Keeping Junk On Premises: It shall be unlawful and a misdemeanor for
any person to keep, permit to be kept or to place or cause to be placed any
junk upon premises owned or occupied by said person or upon any of the streets
or alleys or other public grounds.
   C.   Nuisance Declared; Abatement By City:
      1.   The keeping by any person of junk on premises owned or occupied by
said person or the placing thereof on streets, alleys or public places is
hereby declared to be a nuisance.
      2.   The city may remove or abate such nuisance at the expense of the
property upon which the same exists after giving the owner thereof notice to
remove the same within fifteen (15) days, and the failure of said owner to
remove or cause to be removed said nuisance within said time, and the expense
thereof to the city may be certified to the proper officer of Gooding County
for collection with other taxes as provided by law. (1996 Code §
7-1-6)
4-1-7: DEAD ANIMALS:
Any dead animals or parts of animals on premises in a residential area/district
shall be removed within a twenty four (24) hour period. If such is not removed,
the city shall cause its removal. (1996 Code §
7-1-7)
4-1-8: CHARGES FOR ABATEMENT OF WEEDS AND OTHER NUISANCES:
   A.   Charges Imposed: Charges for mowing of weeds on private property or
eliminating other nuisances described in this chapter shall be the actual cost
to the city for such removal. (1996 Code §
7-1-8; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Failure To Pay Bill; Lien: The property owner shall be billed, and if
debt is not paid in a timely fashion, the city shall cause a lien to be placed
on the property in the amount of the debt. (1996 Code §
7-1-8)
CHAPTER 2
OPEN BURNING
SECTION:
4-2-1: Burning, Incineration Regulated
4-2-2: Types Of Fires Allowed
4-2-3: Prohibited Types Of Open Burning
4-2-4: Penalties; Enforcement
4-2-1: BURNING, INCINERATION REGULATED:
No person shall burn or incinerate any rubbish or garbage, except as
hereinafter provided:
   A.   Incinerators:
      1.   Any person may use an incinerator (as defined by the Department of
Environmental Quality in IDAPA 16.01.01) in the interior of a building or on
the exterior of a building, provided such incinerator meets the requirements of
the Building and Fire Codes, planning and zoning requirements and meets the
approval of Idaho Department of Environmental Quality on emissions.
      2.   The hours of operation of such incinerator shall be between seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. and sunset.
   B.   Outdoor Fireplaces, Barbecue Pits: Nothing herein contained shall be
construed to prohibit the use of outdoor fireplaces, barbecue pits or grills in
preparing food or for recreational purposes, except as listed hereafter. (2010
Code)
4-2-2: TYPES OF FIRES ALLOWED:
No person shall build, ignite, or maintain any outdoor fire of any kind or
character, or for any purpose whatsoever, except as provided herein. The
following types of fires are allowable and shall not require a permit:
   A.   Firefighting personnel for the purpose of combating fires.
   B.   Barbecues or other fires used in the preparation of food.
   C.   Campfires, or fires used for recreational or ceremonial purposes. Fire
extinguishing equipment, such as a water hose connected to a water supply,
shall be readily available. (2010 Code)
   D.   The time for all allowed open burning shall be from seven o'clock (7:
00) A.M. to sunset. (Ord. 1074, 6-7-2017)
4-2-3: PROHIBITED TYPES OF OPEN BURNING:
No person shall allow, suffer, cause, or permit burning of any of the following
types of materials at any time:
   A.   Burn barrels of any kind.
   B.   Household solid waste or garbage.
   C.   Junked motor vehicles or any material resulting from a salvage
operation.
   D.   Tires or other rubber materials or products.
   E.   Insulated wire.
   F.   Plastics.
   G.   Existing structures.
   H.   Asphalt, tarpaper, waste, or heavy petroleum products.
   I.   Lumber or timbers treated with preservatives, lawn clippings.
   J.   Other construction materials such as sheetrock, flooring, insulation.
   K.   Dead animals or parts thereof, except upon the order of a Public Health
Officer to dispose of diseased animals.
   L.   Paint, solvent, or other chemicals including motor oils, diesel,
gasoline, etc.
   M.   Trade waste.
   N.   Pathogenic wastes or infectious wastes, except under order of a Public
Health Officer.
   O.   Hazardous waste, except when burned under order of a public or military
fire chief to dispose of materials (including military ordnance) which present
a danger to life, valuable property, or the public welfare, or for the purpose
of the prevention of a fire hazard when no practical alternative method of
disposal or removal is available.
   P.   Any types of materials that emit large volumes of smoke, particulates,
or odors including wet materials.
   Q.   Any other material that would otherwise be allowed under this chapter,
but is determined to be a nuisance, hazard, or source of air pollution.
   R.   Notwithstanding the provisions of any section of this chapter, any
material which violates and causes an air pollution alert.
   S.   Notwithstanding the provisions of any section of this chapter, any
material that is restricted as specified in IDAPA Rules for the Control of Air
Pollution 16.01.01. (2010 Code)
4-2-4: PENALTIES; ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Penalties Imposed: Failure to comply with any provision of this chapter
shall be a violation of this chapter, and will permit the City to initiate one
or more of the following actions:
      1.   Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be guilty
of an infraction. An infraction shall be punishable as by civil penalty as
provided in subsection
1-4-1B of this Code.
      2.   Legal proceedings to obtain an injunction against the owner of the
property upon which open burning was conducted.
   B.   Enforcement By State: Nothing in this chapter shall preclude the
Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) from enforcing the provisions of the
"Rules for the Control of Air Pollution in Idaho" (IDAPA) 16.01.01, the
Environmental Protection and Health Act, or the Hazardous Waste Management Act
1 . (2010 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 39-101 et seq., and § 39-4401 et seq., respectively.
TITLE 5
PUBLIC SAFETY
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-1-1: General Offense
5-1-2: Concealing Knowledge
5-1-3: Assault And Battery
5-1-4: Disorderly Conduct
5-1-5: Disturbing The Peace
5-1-6: Weapons, Discharge
5-1-7: Drunkenness
5-1-8: Obscene Conduct; Prostitution
5-1-9: Window Peeping
5-1-10: Fraudulently Avoiding Payment Of Admission Fees
5-1-11: False Pretenses
5-1-12: Petit Theft
5-1-13: Swindling
5-1-14: Burglar Tools
5-1-15: Offenses Against Public Authority
5-1-16: Offenses Concerning Assemblages; Riot
5-1-17: Property Related Offenses
5-1-18: Vehicles; Noise Related Offenses
5-1-1: GENERAL OFFENSE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit any act or fail to perform any
requirement which is prohibited or required by state law, insofar as such laws
are applicable to municipal government. (1996 Code §
8-1-17)
5-1-2: CONCEALING KNOWLEDGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to conceal knowledge of the commission of
any offense or to conceal knowledge of any unlawful act as defined in this
code. (1996 Code §
8-1-8)
5-1-3: ASSAULT AND BATTERY:
   A.   Assault: It shall be unlawful for any person to commit "assault" which
is hereby defined as any conduct which places another in reasonable
apprehension of receiving a battery. (1996 Code §
8-1-2)
   B.   Battery: It shall be unlawful for any person to commit battery. A
person commits battery if he intentionally or knowingly, without legal
justification and by any means, causes bodily harm to an individual or makes
physical contact of an insulting or provoking nature with an individual. (1996
Code §
8-1-4)
5-1-4: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
   A.   Indecent Or Insulting Language Or Conduct: It shall be unlawful for any
person to engage in any illegal or improper diversion or to use insulting,
indecent or immoral language, or to be guilty of any indecent, insulting or
immoral conduct or behavior.
   B.   Violent, Noisy Or Disorderly Conduct: Any person who shall be guilty of
any violent, noisy, riotous or disorderly conduct, or who shall use any
profane, abusive or obscene language, or in any way commit a breach of the
peace or do anything that shall be offensive to the senses or dangerous to the
peace of the inhabitants of the city shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor.
   C.   Acts Constituting Disorderly Conduct: Every person shall be guilty of
disorderly conduct when he:
      1.   Solicits anyone to engage in, or engages in, lewd or dissolute
conduct in any public place or in any place open to the public or exposed to
public view.
      2.   Accosts other persons in any public place or in any place open to
the public for the purpose of begging or soliciting alms.
      3.   Loiters in, about or upon any street, alley or other public way or
public place, or in any place open to the public, without lawful business and
conducts himself in a lewd, wanton or lascivious manner in speech or behavior.
      4.   Has upon his person or in his possession any instrument, tool or
other implement for picking locks or pockets or any implement that is usually
employed or that reasonably may be inferred to have been designed to be
employed in the commission of any felony, misdemeanor or the violation of any
ordinance, and who shall fail to account for the possession of same.
      5.   Loiters, remains, or wanders upon the streets or from place to place
without apparent reason or business and who refuses to identify himself and to
account for his presence when requested by a police officer so to do, if the
surrounding circumstances are such to indicate to a reasonable man that the
public safety demands such identification.
      6.   Occupies, lodges or sleeps in any building, structure or place,
whether public or private, or any automobile, truck, railroad car or other
similar vehicles or equipment without the permission of the owner or person
entitled to the possession or in control thereof. (1996 Code §
8-1-9)
      7.   Is found in any public place or in any place open to the public view
under the influence of intoxicating liquor or any drug or any substance defined
as a poison and regulated as a poison, pursuant to the provisions of Idaho Code
title 37, chapter 27, or under the influence of any combination of any
intoxicating liquor, drug or substance, in such a condition that he is unable
to exercise care for his own safety or the safety of others, or by reason of
his being under the influence of intoxicating liquor, or any drug or the
influence of any substance as defined and regulated by said Idaho Code title
37, chapter 27, or under the influence of any combination of any intoxicating
liquor, drug or any such substance, interferes with or obstructs the free use
of any street, sidewalk or other public way or any place open to the public or
exposed to public view.
      8.   Loiters, prowls or wanders upon the private property of another,
without visible or lawful business with the owner or occupants thereof.
      9.   Loiters or remains in or about a school, not having any reason or
relationship involving custody of or responsibility for a pupil or student, or
any other specific, legitimate reason for the same. (1996 Code §
8-1-9; amd. 2010 Code)
5-1-5: DISTURBING THE PEACE:
It shall be unlawful for any person wilfully, maliciously, intentionally or
unnecessarily, to disturb the peace and quiet of another or of any neighborhood
or family or religious congregation or other assembly by loud or unusual noises
or indecent behavior or by offensive or unbecoming conduct, or for any person
to threaten, quarrel, fight or provoke an assault or battery or curse or swear
or utter any obscene or vulgar or indecent language in the presence of another.
(1996 Code §
8-1-10)
5-1-6: WEAPONS, DISCHARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any weapon, air gun, sparrow
gun, flipper, firearm or any similar device or contrivance within the limits of
the city, unless otherwise provided for by law. (1996 Code § 8-1-44)
5-1-7: DRUNKENNESS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to be found drunk, intoxicated or under the
influence of intoxicating liquor upon any public thoroughfare, highway, or upon
any public sidewalk. (1996 Code §
8-1-11; amd. 2010 Code)
5-1-8: OBSCENE CONDUCT; PROSTITUTION:
   A.   Indecent Exposure: It shall be unlawful for any person to appear in a
state of nudity or in any indecent or lewd dress or condition in any public
place, or in any such place to make any indecent exposure of his or her person
or private parts thereof or the private parts of another, or to conduct himself
in a lewd or lascivious manner. (1996 Code §
8-1-18; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Prostitution: It shall be unlawful for any person to pursue or
advertise in any manner his or her vocation as a prostitute or for any person
to advertise the profession of a prostitute or solicit for a prostitute. (1996
Code § 8-1-35)
5-1-9: WINDOW PEEPING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to look, peer or peep into, or to be found
loitering around or within view of, any window not on his property with the
intent of watching or looking through said window. (1996 Code § 8-1-43)
5-1-10: FRAUDULENTLY AVOIDING PAYMENT OF ADMISSION FEES:
It shall be unlawful for any person fraudulently to enter, without payment of
the proper admission fee, any theater, ballroom, lecture, concert or other
place where admission fees are charged; provided, however, that nothing herein
contained shall be deemed to prohibit or restrict the free admission of police
officers engaged in the performance of police duties to any place of public
entertainment or amusement. (1996 Code §
8-1-1)
5-1-11: FALSE PRETENSES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obtain any food, drink, goods, wares or
merchandise under false pretenses, or to enter any public place and call for
refreshments or other articles and receive and refuse to pay for same, or
depart without paying for or satisfying the person from whom he received the
food, goods, wares and merchandise. (1996 Code §
8-1-15)
5-1-12: PETIT THEFT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to commit "petit theft" which is hereby
defined as a theft when the property taken is of a value of less than one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00). (1996 Code § 8-1-29; amd. 2010 Code)
5-1-13: SWINDLING:
It shall be unlawful for any person, by color, or aid or any trick or sleight
of hand performance or by fraud or by fraudulent scheme, cards, dice or device,
to win for himself or for another any money or property or a representative of
either. (1996 Code § 8-1-39)
5-1-14: BURGLAR TOOLS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to have in his or her possession any
nippers of any description known as burglar's nippers, pick lock, skeleton key,
jimmy, or other burglar's instrument or tool of any description, unless it be
shown that the possession is innocent or for a lawful purpose. (1996 Code §
8-1-5)
5-1-15: OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC AUTHORITY:
   A.   Refusal To Assist Police Officers: It shall be unlawful for any person
over the age of eighteen (18) years to refuse or neglect to render assistance
to any police officer when called upon for such assistance or aid in the
suppression of riot or other unlawful assemblage, or in the arrest of any
person who has committed an offense. (1996 Code § 8-1-32; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   False Representation: It shall be unlawful for any person to represent
falsely himself to be an officer of the city or to attempt to impersonate any
such officer or to, without authority, perform any official act therein on
behalf of an officer. (1996 Code §
8-1-16)
   C.   Resisting An Officer: It shall be unlawful for any person to interfere
wilfully with, resist, delay, obstruct, molest or threaten to molest any
officer of the law in the exercise of his official duties. (1996 Code § 8-1-37)
   D.   Escapes:
      1.   Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person convicted of any
offense or in lawful custody to escape or attempt to escape from custody. (1996
Code §
8-1-13)
      2.   Aid: It shall be unlawful for any person to aid or assist any person
to escape from lawful confinement or to assist any person to escape from the
custody of any peace officer. (1996 Code §
8-1-12)
   E.   Removal Of City Barricades, Signs And Notices:
      1.   Removal Of Barricades: It shall be unlawful for any person to remove
or change the placement of any safety or traffic barricade placed on any
sidewalk, alley, street or on any public property or placed lawfully on private
property by a city employee or its agents.
      2.   Removal Of Signs Or Notices: It shall be unlawful for any person to
remove, alter or change any sign or notice posted by the city or its agents
which has been placed lawfully on any public or private property.
      3.   Violation A Misdemeanor: Any person violating provisions of this
subsection shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 1008, 3-22-2000)
5-1-16: OFFENSES CONCERNING ASSEMBLAGES; RIOT:
   A.   Unlawful Assembly: It shall be unlawful for any two (2) or more persons
to assemble together for the purpose of disturbing the peace or for the purpose
of committing an unlawful act and not to disperse upon the command of an
officer so to do. (1996 Code §
8-1-3)
   B.   Collecting Crowds: It shall be unlawful for any person to collect
within the city a crowd of people to the annoyance of the citizens thereof or
to the annoyance or injury of the public. (1996 Code §
8-1-7)
   C.   Riot: It shall be unlawful for any person to fail or refuse immediately
to disperse upon an order to do so by a police officer, when two (2) or more
persons are assembled for the purpose of disturbing the peace or for the
purpose of committing any unlawful act. (1996 Code § 8-1-38)
5-1-17: PROPERTY RELATED OFFENSES:
   A.   Malicious Injury To Property: It shall be unlawful for any person
wilfully and maliciously to injure, deface, mutilate, remove, pull down, break
or in any manner interfere with or molest or secrete or destroy any real or
personal property belonging to or under the control of any person. (1996 Code §
8-1-34)
   B.   Letting Premises For Unlawful Purposes: It shall be unlawful for any
person to rent, use or allow to be used any building or property owned by him,
for any purpose whereby riotous or disorderly persons are gathered. (1996 Code
§
8-1-21)
   C.   Storage Of Junk Restricted: It shall be unlawful for any person to
store or keep any old articles or materials which may be classified as junk
adjacent to or in close proximity to any schoolhouse, church, public parks,
public grounds, business buildings or residences without first providing proper
and tight buildings for the storage of the same. (1996 Code §
8-1-20)
   D.   Streets:
      1.   Injurious Materials On Thoroughfares: It shall be unlawful for any
person to deposit, place or allow to remain in or upon any public thoroughfare
any material or substance injurious to persons or property. (1996 Code §
8-1-19)
      2.   Obstructing Streets: It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct
or cause to be obstructed any of the sidewalks, streets or alleys without first
having obtained permission to do so from the chief of police or street
superintendent. (1996 Code § 8-1-27; amd. 2010 Code)
      3.   Water Flowing Upon Streets: It shall be unlawful for any person to
allow any water to flow into or upon any public thoroughfare. (1996 Code § 8-1-
42)
   E.   Injury To Vehicles: It shall be unlawful for any person to
individually, or in association with one or more others, wilfully break,
injure, tamper with or remove any part or parts of any vehicle for the purpose
of injuring, defacing or destroying such vehicle, or temporarily or permanently
preventing its useful operation, or for any purpose against the will or without
the consent of the owner of such vehicle, or to in any other manner wilfully or
maliciously interfere with or prevent the running or operation of such vehicle.
(1996 Code § 8-1-41)
   F.   Expectorating: It shall be unlawful for any person to expectorate or
spit upon any sidewalk or upon the floor of any public building or room used
for public assemblies. (1996 Code §
8-1-14)
   G.   Trespassing: Covered under Idaho Code section 18-7008. (1996 Code § 8-
1-40)
5-1-18: VEHICLES; NOISE RELATED OFFENSES 1 :
   A.   Vehicles Using Loudspeakers; Sound Trucks: It shall be unlawful to
play, operate or use any devices known as a sound truck, loudspeakers or sound
amplifier, radio or phonograph, with loud and raucous noises and which is
attached to and upon any vehicle unless such person in charge of such vehicle
shall have first applied to and received permission from the city to operate
any such vehicle so equipped. (1996 Code §
8-1-22)
   B.   Mufflers, Unnecessary Noise: It shall be unlawful for any person to
operate a motor vehicle which shall not at all times be equipped with a muffler
upon the exhaust thereof in good working order and in constant operation to
prevent excessive or unusual noise, and it shall be unlawful for any person
operating any motor vehicle to use a cutout, bypass or similar muffler
elimination appliance. (1996 Code §
8-1-24)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  4-1-3 of this code.
CHAPTER 2
MINORS
SECTION:
5-2-1: Curfew
5-2-2: Cigarette Or Tobacco Sales To Minors
5-2-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Age And Hours Restrictions: It shall be unlawful for any person under
the age of eighteen (18) years to be or remain, and it shall be unlawful for
any parent, guardian or other person having care/custody of any person under
the age of eighteen (18) years to permit such person to be or to remain in or
upon any street, alley, public ground, public place or any place open to the
public or exposed to public use within the city between the hours of twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. (Ord. 998, 5-19-1998;
amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Exceptions To Curfew Hours: A minor shall not be subject to curfew
hours under the following conditions:
      1.   When accompanied by their parent, guardian or other adult person.
      2.   When engaged in legitimate employment for profit or going to or
returning home from a legitimate employment activity without any detour or
stops.
      3.   When engaged in the performance of an errand or duty at the
direction of their parent, guardian or other adult person having care and
custody of the minor.
      4.   When attending an official school, religious or other recreational
activity supervised by adults and sponsored by the county, city, school
district, recreational district, any other civic organization, religious
organization or other similar entities that take responsibility for the minor
for going to or returning home from, without any detour or stops, an official
school, religious or other recreational activity supervised by adults and
sponsored by one of the entities previously stated.
      5.   When involved in an emergency, which includes, but is not limited
to, a fire, natural disaster, automobile accident or any situation requiring
immediate action to protect personal injury or loss of life.
      6.   When emancipated by marriage, or a minor who is in active military
service.
      7.   When exercising first amendment rights protected by the United
States constitution such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech
and the right to assemble.
   C.   Violation A Misdemeanor: Any person violating a provision of this
section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 998, 5-19-1998)
5-2-2: CIGARETTE OR TOBACCO SALES TO MINORS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or give away, directly or
indirectly, to any person under the age of eighteen (18) years, any cigarettes,
tobacco, or any compounds of tobacco used in filling up or making up of a
cigarette, or to give or sell any cigarette papers to minors. (1996 Code §
8-1-6)
ARTICLE A. PARENTAL RESPONSIBILITY
SECTION:
5-2A-1: Title, Structure, Purpose And Authority
5-2A-2: Definitions
5-2A-3: Failure To Supervise
5-2A-4: Exceptions
5-2A-5: Violations; Penalties
5-2A-1: TITLE, STRUCTURE, PURPOSE AND AUTHORITY:
   A.   Short Title: This article shall be known as the CITY OF HAGERMAN
PARENTAL RESPONSIBILITY ORDINANCE.
   B.   Structure: Titles and subtitles of this article are only used for
organization and structure and the language in each paragraph of this article
should control with regard to determining the legislative intent and meaning of
the city council.
   C.   Purpose: The purpose of this article is as follows:
      1.   To provide for and further the health, safety and welfare of the
public.
      2.   To protect juveniles' health and welfare, which includes their care,
guidance and control.
      3.   To reduce instances of juvenile crime.
      4.   To encourage parents, guardians, or other persons, except foster
parents, to properly supervise and control children under sixteen (16) years of
age who are in their care and custody.
      5.   To hold parents, guardians, or other persons, except a foster
parent, who are lawfully charged with the care or custody of a child under
sixteen (16) years of age for failing to supervise the child over whom they
have responsibility.
   D.   Authority: This article is enacted pursuant to authority conferred by
article XII, section 2 of the Idaho constitution and Idaho Code sections 31-
714, 31-828, and 32-1301. (Ord. 999, 5-19-1998)
5-2A-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this article, the following terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
CHILD: A person under sixteen (16) years of age.
PARENT: Any person who is the parent, lawful guardian or other person, except
the foster parent, lawfully charged with the care or custody of the child under
sixteen (16) years of age. (Ord. 999, 5-19-1998)
5-2A-3: FAILURE TO SUPERVISE:
It is declared unlawful for a person who is the parent, lawful guardian or
other person, except a foster parent, lawfully charged with the care or custody
of a child under sixteen (16) years of age to fail to supervise that child. The
parent commits the offense of failure to supervise a child if the child commits
any of the following acts:
   A.   Commits any act bringing the child within the purview of the juvenile
corrections act, Idaho Code title 20, chapter 5; or
   B.   Commits a crime for which the child is to be tried as an adult; or
   C.   Commits an act for which jurisdiction of the juvenile corrections act
is subject to waiver pursuant to Idaho Code title 20, chapter 5; or
   D.   Fails to attend school or is not comparably instructed as provided in
Idaho Code section 33-202; or
   E.   Violates the city curfew ordinance or the curfew laws of any city
within Gooding County 1 . (Ord. 999, 5-19-1998)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  5-2-1 of this chapter.
5-2A-4: EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   A person shall not be subject to prosecution for violation of this
article if the person:
      1.   Is the victim of the act bringing the child within the purview of
the provisions of Idaho Code title 20, chapter 5; or
      2.   Reported the act of the child as soon as reasonably possible to a
local law enforcement agency, juvenile court, or the department of health and
welfare.
   B.   A person shall not be subject to prosecution for violation of this
article if the person shows to the satisfaction of the court that the person
took reasonable steps to control the conduct of the child at the time the
person is alleged to have failed to supervise the child. (Ord. 999, 5-19-1998)
5-2A-5: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Penalty Imposed; Parenting Classes: A violation of any of the
provisions of this article is a misdemeanor, and any person who is found guilty
or pleads guilty to a violation of this article shall be subject to a fine of
not more than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). In lieu of imposing a fine, the
court, with the consent of the person, may order the person to complete
parenting classes or undertake other treatment or counseling to the
satisfaction of the court. The court may discharge the person or, if the person
fails to complete the programs to the satisfaction of the court, the court may
impose the penalty provided in this section.
   B.   Contempt Proceedings: Any person violating any order of the court
entered under this article shall be subject to contempt proceedings in
accordance with Idaho Code title 7, chapter 6, in addition to any other
penalties authorized pursuant to this section.
   C.   Payment Of Restitution: Any person who is found guilty or pleads guilty
to a violation of this article may be ordered by the court to pay restitution
or make whole any victim who suffers an economic loss as a result of the
juvenile's conduct, in accordance with the standards and requirements of Idaho
Code sections 19-5304 and 19-5305; provided, that any restitution ordered to be
paid by a parent under this article shall not exceed two thousand five hundred
dollars ($2,500.00).
   D.   Service Of Copy Of Article: Upon a first offense, a law enforcement
officer may, in his discretion, serve a copy of this article upon the parents
and explain to them the consequences of their conduct as a warning of the
penalties contained in this article. This service shall be documented by the
officer.
   E.   Other Actions Or Proceedings: A conviction of a person under this
article shall not preclude any other action or proceedings against the person
which may be taken pursuant to the provisions of Idaho Code title 20, chapter
5, or other provisions of law. (Ord. 999, 5-19-1998)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
SECTION:
5-3-1: Number Of Dogs Limited; Licensing Requirements; Fees
5-3-2: Running At Large Prohibited
5-3-3: Nuisances And Dangerous And At-Risk Dogs Prohibited
5-3-4: Rabid Animals Quarantined For Observation
5-3-5: Cruelty To Animals
5-3-6: Poisoning Unlawful
5-3-7: Domestic Livestock
5-3-8: Impoundment And Redemption Procedures
5-3-9: Enforcement Powers And Duties
5-3-10: Liability For Damage To Property
5-3-11: Penalty
5-3-1: NUMBER OF DOGS LIMITED; LICENSING REQUIREMENTS; FEES:
   A.   A Maximum Number Of Dogs: No household, individual, or business shall
possess, harbor or own more than three (3) dogs, over the age of (6) months,
within the city limits.
      1.   Military Exemption: If a resident of the City of Hagerman is
supporting an active-duty immediate family member who owns a dog, that resident
may harbor the dog owned by the immediate family member while they are serving
active duty. However, in no event shall the total number of dogs exceed four
(4) dogs per household. The harborer of the dog will provide to the City of
Hagerman: proof of ownership, proof of active duty, current certificate of
rabies, current license with the City of Hagerman, and demonstrate the ability
to keep the dog safe and within the nuisance laws stated under the City of
Hagerman City Code Section
5-3-3.
   B.   License And Registration For Dogs:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to own, harbor, keep or possess
a dog more than six (6) months old, within the City without first procuring a
license as provided by this chapter; provided, however that the provisions of
this section shall not apply to any person visiting the City for a period not
to exceed thirty (30) days, and owning and possessing a dog currently licensed,
and bearing the current license issued by another municipality, or other
governmental licensing authority.
      2.   The dog license shall be issued by the City Clerk-Treasurer upon
payment of a license fee as herein provided. Payment of a license fee shall be
made to the City Clerk-Treasurer at City Hall during regular business hours.
The license fees shall be set by resolution of the City Council.
      3.   Such license shall be paid annually by December 31. All licenses
shall expire on December 31 of each year and no notice shall be sent by the
City of Hagerman concerning the expiration of the license. A late fee will be
imposed after January 31st. The late fee shall be set by resolution of the City
Council.
   C.   Licensing And Registration Requirement:
      1.   Application; Fee; Proof Of Vaccination: The owner or harborer of any
dog six (6) months of age or older shall make application for and obtain a
license and registration tag for each dog. At the time of making application,
the owner or harborer of any dog shall:
         a.   Provide the name, address, current phone number, sex, breed, and
color of each dog owned or harbored by such person and if the dog is spayed or
neutered.
         b.   Pay a license fee for each dog license.
         c.   Provide proof of current rabies vaccination for the dog being
licensed.
         d.   Upon payment of the license fee and upon providing a current
rabies certificate, the City Clerk/Treasurer shall issue the owner a license
certificate and a metallic tag for each dog so licensed. The licenses shall be
issued in four (4) categories as follows:
         One (1) year license for neutered or spayed animals requiring a three
(3) year rabies certificate.
         A three (3) year license for neutered or spayed animals requiring a
three (3) year rabies certificate.
         One (1) year license for un-neutered or un-spayed animals requiring a
one (1) year or three (3) year rabies certificate.
         A three (3) year license for un-neutered or un-spayed animals
requiring a three (3) year rabies certificate.
      2.   Certificate And Tag; Collar Required; Duplicate Tag:
         a.   Upon payment of the license fee and proof of rabies vaccination,
the City Clerk-Treasurer shall issue the owner a certificate and a metallic tag
for each dog so licensed.
         b.   Every owner or harborer shall be required to provide each dog
with a collar to which the license tag must be affixed, and worn by the dog at
all times.
         c.   In case a dog tag is lost or destroyed, a duplicate tag will be
issued by the City upon presentation of the registration for the current year
and an additional payment of such amount as set by resolution of the City
Council for a duplicate tag.
         d.   Dog tags shall not be transferable from one (1) dog to another
and no refunds shall be made for any dog license due to death of the dog or the
owner of the animal moving from the City before the expiration of the license.
         e.   Service Dogs; License Required; Fee Waived: Any dog which has
been trained to assist the handicapped and is currently acting in that capacity
shall be licensed; however, the owner shall be exempt from paying the license
fee for such dog.
   D.   Dog Kennels Prohibited:
      1.   Unless otherwise provided in the city zoning regulations, no
individual or business shall operate or maintain a kennel within the city. A
"kennel" is defined in section
10-2-2 of this code.
      2.   The kennel restriction as contained in this section shall not apply
to the city or to any veterinarian clinic or hospital located within the city.
(Ord. 1037, 3-21-2007; amd. 2010 Code; Ord. 1091, 5-5-2021)
5-3-2: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED:
   A.   Private Premises Or Public Places: It shall be unlawful for any owner,
possessor or person who keeps any dog to permit the same to run at large upon
the private premises of others or upon the streets, alleys, sidewalks,
highways, vacant lots, school grounds or other public places within the city.
(1996 Code §
8-2-1)
   B.   Running At Large Described; Exceptions:
      1.   A dog shall be deemed to be running at large when off or away from
the premises of the owner, possessor, or keeper thereof, and not under the
immediate control of such owner, possessor, or keeper thereof or his agent or
servant or a member of his immediate family either by leash, cord or chain;
provided, however, that any dog on the premises of a city park or school
grounds must be controlled. (1996 Code §
8-2-1; amd. 2010 Code)
      2.   Procuring a license and tag shall not authorize the running at large
of said dog.
      3.   This provision shall not apply to dogs working with livestock or to
dogs, engaged with their owner, in hunting or performing in field trials.
   C.   Violations Declared A Nuisance: Violation of the provisions of this
section is hereby declared to be a nuisance and a menace to the public health
and safety, and said dog or dogs shall be taken up and impounded as provided
herein. (1996 Code §
8-2-1)
5-3-3: NUISANCES AND DANGEROUS AND AT-RISK DOGS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Creating A Nuisance; Barking Or Attacking: It shall be unlawful for any
owner or other keeper of a dog or other animal to fail to exercise proper care
and control of such animal to prevent it from becoming a public nuisance.
Frequent, continuous or untimely barking, molesting passersby, chasing
vehicles, habitually attacking other domestic animals, trespassing upon public
or private property in such manner as to damage the property shall be deemed a
nuisance.
   B.   Dangerous Dogs: Anyone that harbors or keeps a "Dangerous Dog", which
for purposes of Title 5, Chapter 3 of this code is defined as a dog that
without Justified Provocation bites a person causing injury, is guilty of a
misdemeanor and subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. "Justified Provocation" means to perform any act or
omission that a reasonable person with common knowledge of dog behavior would
conclude is likely to precipitate a bite or attack by an ordinary dog and shall
include but not be limited to the following:
      1.   The dog was protecting or defending a person within the immediate
vicinity of the dog from an attack or assault;
      2.   The person was committing a crime or offense upon the property of
the owner or custodian of the dog;
      3.   The person was at the time, or had in the past, willfully tormented,
abused or assaulted the dog;
      4.   The dog was responding to pain or injury or protecting its
offspring;
      5.   The dog was working as a hunting dog, herding dog, or predator
control dog on the property of, or under the control of, its owner or keeper,
and the damage or injury sustained was to a person who was interfering with the
dog while the dog was working in a place where it was lawfully engaged in such
activity, including public lands;
      6.   The dog was a service animal individually trained to do work or
perform tasks for a person with a disability; or
      7.   The person was intervening between two (2) or more animals engaged
in aggressive behavior or fighting.
   C.   Dangerous Dogs At Large: If any Dangerous Dog is found at large which
cannot be taken up and impounded, such dog may be slain by any Sheriff's
Officer or Animal Control Officer.
   D.   Nothing in this subsection
5-3-3 is intended to alter, replace, or affect the provisions and requirements
of Idaho Code section 25-2810.
(Ord. 1099, 11- -2023)
5-3-4: RABID ANIMALS QUARANTINED FOR OBSERVATION:
   A.   Quarantine:
      1.   A dog which is known to have bitten, or injured, any person so as to
cause an abrasion of the skin, or a suspected rabid dog, shall be placed in
confinement under observation of the veterinary hospital, or municipal pound,
and shall not be killed or released until at least ten (10) days after the
onset of symptoms suggestive of rabies.
      2.   Any animal of the species subject to rabies that has bitten a person
shall likewise be confined and observed for at least ten (10) days. (1996 Code
§
8-2-7)
      3.   If the animal dies or has been killed, its head shall be removed and
immediately taken to the Boise Animal Health Laboratory to be examined for
rabies. (1996 Code §
8-2-7; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   Official Inspection Or Examination; Determination:
      1.   No person shall fail, refuse or neglect to allow any official of the
City to make an inspection or examination thereof at any time during said
period.
      2.   No such dog or animal shall be removed from the place of quarantine
without written permission of the City.
      3.   If the animal shall be determined free of rabies, the same shall be
returned to the owner upon payment of a fee to be designated by the animal
control officer for keeping dogs impounded. No other fee shall be charged; if
such fee is not paid, the dog shall be subject to disposal. (1996 Code §
8-2-7)
5-3-5: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
   A.   Failing To Provide Sustenance: It shall be unlawful for any owner or
other keeper of an animal to fail to provide such animal with sufficient and
wholesome food and water, proper shelter and protection, veterinary care when
needed to prevent suffering, or humane care and treatment. (1996 Code §
8-2-2)
   B.   Inhumane Treatment: It shall be unlawful for any person to maltreat or
torture any dog or other animal, or, having the right or authority to kill any
dog or other animal, to kill such dog or other animal in an inhumane manner.
(1996 Code § 8-2-9)
5-3-6: POISONING UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful for any person to administer or cause to be administered
poison of any sort whatsoever to any animal which is the property of another,
or poison food where same is accessible to any dog or other animal. (1996 Code
§ 8-2-10; amd. 2010 Code)
5-3-7: DOMESTIC LIVESTOCK:
   A.   Livestock Prohibited: It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and
unlawful for any person to keep or maintain horses, mules, cattle, sheep,
goats, pigs, fowl, or similar livestock, within the City Limits.
   B.   Exception:
      1.   Laying Hens: Each household in the City of Hagerman shall be allowed
to possess up to six (6) laying hens to be kept in the back yard of a residence
subject to the following conditions:
         a.   Permitted Location: Kept in a fenced back yard of a residence.
         b.   Roosters Prohibited: No roosters are allowed.
         c.   Running At Large Prohibited: Not allowed to run at large.
         d.   Prohibited Locations: Not allowed in front or side yards of the
residence.
         e.   Noncommercial Use Only: Kept for noncommercial use only, such as
for family consumption, or 4-H or school projects, etc.
      2.   Market Lamb Projects: That each household in the City of Hagerman
shall be allowed to possess two (2) lambs for the purpose of a market lamb
project for 4-H or, FFA, provided that the household has sufficient pasture
area to contain the lambs without creating a nuisance and the market lambs are
in the personal possession and responsibility of the child who will be the
primary caretaker of the lambs. In the event that any individual wishes to have
more than (2) lambs, for a market lamb project, then they may apply to the City
for a special use permit for the excess number of lambs.
      3.   Special Use Permit: Any individual who resides within the City
limits who wishes to have market lambs in excess of two (2) lambs, for any
market lamb project, may apply for a special use permit for the additional
lambs as long as those lambs are in the personal possession and responsibility
of the child who will be the primary caretaker of the market lambs. The permit
shall be issued for a period of time not to exceed not more than six (6)
months. A new permit must be applied for each year. The fee for the permit
shall be five dollars ($5.00) per lamb in excess of two (2) lambs.
   C.   Existing Pasture: Existing pastures shall remain a pasture until the
pasture is void of any lambs for more than six (6) months. The minimum size for
a pasture shall be two (2) City lots or twelve thousand five hundred (12,500)
square feet. (1996 Code § 8-2-15; amd. Ord. 1063, 4-16-2014; Ord. 1091, 5-5-
2021)
5-3-8: IMPOUNDMENT AND REDEMPTION PROCEDURES:
   A.   Authority To Impound: Any animal control officer or any other person
authorized by the City may, in fresh pursuit, seize and impound all dogs
without collars bearing licenses as required by this chapter, or any and all
dogs or any other animals found running at large upon the public streets,
alleys or other public places or private premises without the permission of the
owner of said premises.
   B.   Hearing Regarding Impounded Animals: A hearing may be held at the
request of any animal owner whose animal has been impounded. Said hearing shall
be requested by contacting the Mayor, and shall be requested within forty-
eight (48) hours of said impoundment.
   C.   Redemption:
      1.   Any dog impounded may be taken from the pound by the owner or any
authorized person upon exhibiting to the animal control officer or authorized
person having charge of said pound a receipt showing that the license fee has
been paid for such dog, and upon paying the person in charge of the pound an
impounding fee to be set by resolution of the City Council.
      2.   All impounded dogs not redeemed within seventy-two (72) hours shall
be offered for adoption to a party other than the predetermined prior owner, if
any. Such adoption fee is set by resolution, plus any required license fee.
      3.   All dogs that are not adopted or redeemed within five (5) days may
be destroyed in a humane manner and all expenses will be charged to the owner,
harborer, orkeeper of said animal for the keeping and disposing of said animal.
(1996 Code §§ 8-2-3, 8-2-4, 8-2-12; amd. Ord. 995, 7-15-1997; Ord. 1091, 5-5-
2021)
5-3-9: ENFORCEMENT POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   Animal Control Officer Enforcement: It shall be the duty of the Animal
Control Officer or such persons designated by the City to:
      1.   Enforce the licensing and control the dogs in the City as provided
in this chapter;
      2.   File complaints in the Magistrate Court against any person, firm or
corporation failing to license any dog as provided in this chapter; or who
otherwise fails to comply with any of the provisions of this chapter;
      3.   Capture and secure all dogs found running at large contrary to the
provisions of this chapter;
      4.   Remove such dogs in a humane manner to the pound; and
      5.   Hold dogs as impounded for a period of not less than seventy-two
(72) hours in a humane manner.
   B.   Right Of Entry On Private Property: In the enforcement of any provision
of this chapter, any Deputy Sheriff and the Animal Control Officer or such
persons designated by the City are authorized to enter, while in fresh pursuit,
the private property of any person to take possession of any licensed or
unlicensed, fierce, dangerous, or vicious dog at the time the dog goes onto
private property. 1996 Code §§ 8-2-5, 8-2-11; amd. Ord. 1091, 5-5-2021)
5-3-10: LIABILITY FOR DAMAGE TO PROPERTY:
The owner, harborer or keeper of any dog that does damage to property of
another shall be liable to the owner of the property damaged for the damages
and costs of suit. In the prosecution of action for such damage, it is not
necessary for the plaintiff to show that the owner, harborer or keeper of such
dog had knowledge of the fact that such dog was doing damage to the property.
(1996 Code § 8-2-14)
5-3-11: PENALTY:
Except as otherwise provided in this Title 5, Chapter 3 of this ordinance, any
owner, possessor, or person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be,
upon Conviction or entry of plea, found guilty of an infraction and subject to
a fine of fifty dollars ($50.00) for the first offense and one hundred dollars
($100.00) for any subsequent violations, within a twelve (12) month period. The
third offense within a twelve (12) month period will be charged with a
misdemeanor.
(Ord. 1099, 11- -2023)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC CODE; GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: State Motor Vehicle Laws Adopted
6-1-2: Speed Limits; General
6-1-2-1: Speed Limits; School Zones
6-1-3: Engine Brakes Banned
6-1-4: Removal Of Vehicles
6-1-1: STATE MOTOR VEHICLE LAWS ADOPTED:
   A.   Intent: It is hereby declared to be the intent of the governing body of
the city to aid and assist by whatever means possible, for the utmost
consistency in traffic regulation among and between agencies of Idaho having
such jurisdiction. Toward that end, adoption of the Idaho motor vehicle laws by
the cities of Idaho is a necessary means of assuring maximum uniformity. (1996
Code §
9-1-1)
   B.   Adoption Of State Laws By Reference: There is hereby adopted,
therefore, for the purpose of establishing rules and regulations for the use of
all streets and public thoroughfares of the city, that certain code, identified
as the latest edition of the Idaho motor vehicle laws, more particularly Idaho
Code title 49, published by the department of Idaho state police, and as the
same may hereafter be revised by the Idaho legislature, or amended by the
governing body, and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated as an ordinance
of the city as fully as though set forth at length herein. (1996 Code §
9-1-1; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Copy On File: A copy of the said Idaho motor vehicle laws, together
with any revisions or amendments, duly certified by the city clerk-treasurer,
shall be kept on file at city hall for use and examination of and by the
public. (1996 Code §
9-1-1)
6-1-2: SPEED LIMITS; GENERAL:
   A.   Limits Established:
      1.   General: Unless otherwise set forth in this section, the maximum
speed limit on any street, alley and State Highway 30 within the city limits
shall be twenty five (25) miles per hour. (Ord. 1049, 6-16-2010)
   B.   Violations A Misdemeanor: Any person violating any provision of this
section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 1000, 6-2-1998)
6-1-2-1: SPEED LIMITS; SCHOOL ZONES:
   A.   Speed Limit: Speed limit for all residential school zones shall be
twenty (20) miles per hour. Speed limits for the U.S. Highway 30 school zones
shall be twenty five (25) miles per hour. The time of enforcement for all
school zone speed limits shall be between seven thirty o'clock (7:30) A.M. and
four o'clock (4:00) P.M. Monday through Friday when school is in session.
School zones speed limit is also in effect during school activities when
students are present.
   B.   School Zones, Residential: Residential school zones shall be the
streets as follows: Second Avenue from the Main Street to Spring Street; Lake
Street from Second Avenue to State Street; Spring Street from Second Avenue to
State Street and Main Street from Second Avenue to State Street.
   C.   School Zones, U.S. Highway 30: School zones located on U.S. Highway 30
in the city of Hagerman shall be between Spring Street and Salmon Street.
   D.   Violation: Any person violating any provision of this section shall be
subject to an infraction citation under Idaho Code 49-658. (Ord. 1052, 10-20-
2010)
6-1-3: ENGINE BRAKES BANNED:
   A.   Prohibition: It shall be unlawful to use air compression brakes,
commonly known as engine brakes within the city limits.
   B.   Penalty: Any person who violates this section shall be guilty of an
infraction and punishable by a fine of fifty dollars ($50.00). (Ord. 1020, 6-3-
2003)
6-1-4: REMOVAL OF VEHICLES:
   A.   Improperly Parked Vehicles: Any vehicle parked in violation of traffic
regulations or any vehicle parked so as to obstruct the free movement of
traffic or to cause a traffic hazard may be immediately removed upon order of a
duly authorized law enforcement officer in accordance with Idaho Code section
49-1801 et seq. (1996 Code §
9-5-1)
   B.   Wrecked Or Abandoned Vehicles: All other vehicles believed to be
abandoned shall be removed in accordance with the provisions of Idaho Code
title 49, chapter 18. (1996 Code §
9-5-2)
CHAPTER 2
TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES
SECTION:
6-2-1: Authority To Install
6-2-2: Specifications
6-2-3: Obedience To Devices
6-2-4: When Devices Required
6-2-5: Unauthorized Signs, Signals Or Markings
6-2-6: Interference With Devices
6-2-7: Crosswalks And Safety Zones
6-2-8: Traffic Lanes
6-2-1: AUTHORITY TO INSTALL:
The city shall place and maintain traffic control signs, signals and devices
when and as required under the traffic regulations of the city to make
effective the provisions of said regulations, and may place and maintain such
additional traffic control devices as may be deemed necessary. (1996 Code §
9-3-1)
6-2-2: SPECIFICATIONS:
All traffic control signs, signals and devices shall conform to the approved
specifications. All signs and signals, required hereunder for a particular
purpose, shall, so far as practicable, be uniform as to type and location
throughout the city. All traffic control devices so erected and not
inconsistent with the provisions of this title shall be official traffic
control devices. (1996 Code §
9-3-2)
6-2-3: OBEDIENCE TO DEVICES:
The driver of any vehicle shall obey the instructions of any official traffic
control device applicable thereto placed in accordance with the traffic
regulations of the city, unless otherwise directed by a police officer, subject
to the exceptions granted the driver of an authorized emergency vehicle. (1996
Code §
9-3-3)
6-2-4: WHEN DEVICES REQUIRED:
No provisions of this title for which signs are required shall be enforced
against an alleged violator if at the time and place of the alleged violation
an official sign is not in proper position and sufficiently legible to be seen
by an ordinarily observant person. Whenever a particular section does not state
that signs are required, such section shall be effective even though no signs
are erected or in place. (1996 Code § 9-3-4)
6-2-5: UNAUTHORIZED SIGNS, SIGNALS OR MARKINGS:
   A.   Prohibited Signs: No person shall place, maintain or display upon or in
view of any highway any authorized sign, signal, marking or device which
purports to be or is an imitation of or resembles an official traffic control
device or railroad sign or signal, or which attempts to direct the movement of
traffic, or which hides from view or interferes with the effectiveness of any
official traffic control device or any railroad sign or signal.
   B.   Commercial Advertising: No person shall place or maintain nor shall any
public authority permit upon any highway any traffic sign or signal bearing
thereon any commercial advertising.
   C.   Exception: This section shall not be deemed to prohibit the erection
upon private property adjacent to highways of signs giving useful directional
information and of a type that cannot be mistaken for official signs.
   D.   Prohibited Signs A Nuisance: Every such prohibited sign, signal or
marking is hereby declared to be a public nuisance and the authority having
jurisdiction over the highway is hereby empowered to remove the same or cause
it to be removed without notice. (1996 Code § 9-3-5)
6-2-6: INTERFERENCE WITH DEVICES:
It shall be unlawful for any person, without lawful authority, to attempt to or
in fact alter, deface, injure, knock down or remove any official traffic
control device or any railroad sign or signal or any inscription, shield or
insignia thereon or any part thereof. (1996 Code § 9-3-6)
6-2-7: CROSSWALKS AND SAFETY ZONES:
The city is hereby authorized:
   A.   Crosswalks: To designate and maintain appropriate devices, marks or
lines upon the surface of the roadway, crosswalks at intersections where, in
the mayor's and city council's opinion there is particular danger to
pedestrians crossing the roadway and at such other places as may be deemed
necessary.
   B.   Safety Zones: To establish safety zones of such kind and character and
at such places as may be deemed necessary for the protection of pedestrians.
(1996 Code § 9-3-7)
6-2-8: TRAFFIC LANES:
   A.   Marking Traffic Lanes: The city is hereby authorized to mark traffic
lanes upon the roadway of any street or highway where a regular alignment of
traffic is necessary.
   B.   Compliance Required: Where such traffic lanes have been marked, it
shall be unlawful for the operator of any vehicle to fail or refuse to keep
such vehicle within the boundaries of such lane except when lawfully passing
another vehicle or preparatory to making a lawful turning movement. (1996 Code
§ 9-3-8)
CHAPTER 3
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Restricted Parking District Established
6-3-2: Parking Lanes Designated
6-3-3: Overparking
6-3-4: Parking Outside Marked Lanes
6-3-5: Parking In Alley
6-3-6: Parking Vehicles With Offensive Loads
6-3-7: Stopping On Crosswalk
