hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance, or create any hazard in
the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant, including, but not limited
to, cyanides in excess of two milligrams per liter (2 mg/l) as CN in the wastes
as discharged to the public sewer.
      3.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to structures, equipment
and personnel of the sewage works.
      4.   Solid or viscous substances in quantities or of such size capable of
causing obstruction to the flow in sewers, or other interference with the
proper operation of the sewage works such as, but not limited to, ashes,
cinders, sand, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags, feathers, tar,
plastics, wood, unground garbage, whole blood, paunch manure, hair and
fleshings, entrails and paper dishes, cups, milk containers, etc., either whole
or ground by garbage grinders.
   D.   Harmful Materials Prohibited In Sewers: No person shall discharge or
cause to be discharged the following described substances, materials, waters or
wastes if it appears likely in the opinion of the superintendent that such
wastes can harm either the sewers, sewage treatment process, or equipment; have
an adverse effect on the receiving stream, or otherwise endanger life, limb,
public property or constitute a nuisance. In forming his opinion as to the
acceptability of these wastes, the superintendent will give consideration to
such factors as to quantities of subject wastes in relation to flows and
velocities in the sewers, materials of construction of the sewers, nature of
the sewage treatment process, capacity of the sewage treatment plant, degree of
treatability of wastes in the sewage treatment plant, and other pertinent
factors. The substances prohibited are:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (65°C).
      2.   Any waters or wastes containing fats, gas, grease or oils, whether
emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter (100 mg/l) or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures
between thirty two (32) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (0 and
65°C).
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage grinder equipped with a motor of three-fourths (3/
4) horsepower (0.76 hp metric), or greater, shall be subject to the review and
approval of the superintendent.
      4.   Any waters or wastes containing strong acid iron pickling wastes, or
concentrated plating solutions whether neutralized or not.
      5.   Any waters or wastes containing iron, chromium, copper, zinc, and
similar objectionable or toxic substances; or wastes exerting an excessive
chlorine requirement, to such degree that any such material received in the
composite sewage at the sewage treatment works exceeds the limits established
by the superintendent for such materials.
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing phenols or other taste or odor
producing substances, in such concentrations exceeding limits which may be
established by the superintendent as necessary, after treatment of the
composite sewage, to meet the requirements of the state, federal or other
public agencies of jurisdiction for such discharge to the receiving waters.
      7.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or
concentrations as may exceed limits established by the superintendent in
compliance with applicable state or federal regulations.
      8.   Any waters or wastes having a pH in excess of 9.5.
      9.   Materials which exert or cause:
         a.   Unusual concentrations or inert suspended solids (such as, but
not limited to, fuller's earth, lime slurries and lime residues) or of
dissolved solids (such as, but not limited to, sodium chloride and sodium
sulfate).
         b.   Excessive BOD, chemical oxygen demand, or chlorine requirements
in such quantities as to constitute a significant load on the sewage treatment
works.
         c.   Excessive discoloration (such as, but not limited to, dye wastes
and vegetable tanning solutions).
         d.   Unusual volume of flow or concentration of wastes constituting
slugs.
      10.   Waters or wastes containing substances which are not amenable to
treatment or reduction by the sewage treatment process employed, or are
amenable to treatment only to such degree that the sewage treatment plant
effluent cannot meet the requirement of other agencies having jurisdiction over
discharge to the receiving waters.
If any waters or wastes are discharged, or are proposed to be discharged into
the public sewers, which waters contain the substances or the characteristics
enumerated in this subsection, and which, in the judgment of the
superintendent, may have a deleterious effect upon the sewage works, processes,
equipment, or receiving waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to life or
constitute a public nuisance, the superintendent may:
         a.   Reject the wastes;
         b.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to
the public sewer;
         c.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/
or
         d.   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating
the wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges under the provisions
of section
8-2-3 of this chapter.
If the superintendent permits the pretreatment or equalization of waste flows,
the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be subject to the
review and approval of the superintendent, and subject to the requirements of
all applicable codes, ordinances and laws.
   E.   Grease, Oil And Sand Interceptors: Grease, oil and sand interceptors
shall be provided when, in the opinion of the superintendent, they are
necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes, sand or other harmful
ingredients; except that, such interceptors shall not be required for private
living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a type and
capacity approved by the superintendent, and shall be located as to be readily
and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection.
   F.   Owner Maintain Preliminary Treatment Or Flow Equalizing Facilities:
Where preliminary treatment or flow equalizing facilities are provided for any
waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory and
effective operation by the owner at his expense.
   G.   Owner Install Control Manhole: When required by the superintendent, the
owner of any property served by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes
shall install a suitable control manhole together with such necessary meters
and other appurtenances in the building sewer to facilitate observation,
sampling and measurement of the wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be
accessibly and safely located, and shall be constructed in accordance with
plans approved by the superintendent. The manhole shall be installed by the
owner at his expense, and shall be maintained by him so as to be safe and
accessible at all times.
   H.   Sampling, Control Manholes: All measurements, tests and analyses of the
characteristics of water and wastes to which reference is made in this section
shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of "Standard Methods
For The Examination Of Water and Wastewater", published by the American Public
Health Association, and shall be determined at the control manhole provided, or
upon suitable samples taken at said control manhole. In the event that no
special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be considered to
be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which the
building sewer is connected. Sampling shall be carried out by customarily
accepted methods to reflect the effect of constituents upon the sewage works
and to determine the existence of hazards to life, limb and property. (The
particular analyses involved will determine whether a 24 hour composite of all
outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample or samples
should be taken. Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids analyses
are obtained from 24 hour composites of all outfalls whereas pHs are determined
from periodic grab samples.)
   I.   Acceptance Of Special Agreements: No statement in this section shall be
construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement between the city
and any industrial concern whereby an industrial waste of unusual strength or
character may be accepted by the city for treatment, subject to payment
therefor by the industrial concern. (1996 Code § 6-4-7)
8-2-8: PRIVIES, CESSPOOLS PROHIBITED; EXCEPTION; PERMIT:
It shall be unlawful for any person to dig or use, or cause to be dug or used,
any privy vault or cesspool or connect any plumbing with a cesspool, or build,
or cause to be built any privy building within the city limits, except upon
written permit of the city council. All applications for such permits must be
in writing and accompanied by a certificate from the council that said premises
are not within three hundred feet (300') of a public sewer. (1996 Code § 6-4-6)
CHAPTER 3
SANITARY SERVICE SYSTEM
SECTION:
8-3-1: Short Title
8-3-2: Definitions
8-3-3: Mandatory Service
8-3-4: Collection And Disposal Requirements; Unlawful Practices
8-3-5: License, Contract Or Franchise
8-3-6: Sanitary Containers
8-3-7: Precollection Practices
8-3-8: Curbside Or Alley Collection; Frequency Of Collection
8-3-9: Rates, Fees, Charges And Deposits
8-3-10: Solid Waste Collection Vehicles; Inspection
8-3-11: Separation And Recycling
8-3-12: Penalty For Infraction
8-3-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the MUNICIPAL SANITARY SYSTEM
OF THE CITY. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following terms, phrases and words shall
have the meanings given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words
used in the present tense include the future, words in the plural number
include the singular, and words in the singular number include the plural. The
word "shall" is always mandatory and not merely directory.
ASHES: The residue from the burning of wood, coal, coke or other combustible
materials.
BULKY WASTE: Stoves, refrigerators, water tanks, washing machines, furniture
and other waste materials other than construction debris, dead animals,
hazardous materials or stable matter with weights or volumes greater than those
allowed for cans.
CAN: A receptacle approved by the city.
CITY: The city of Hagerman, Idaho.
CONSTRUCTION DEBRIS: Waste building materials resulting from construction,
remodeling, repair or demolition operations.
CONTRACTOR: The person or entity authorized by the city to operate, conduct,
and maintain a municipal solid waste collection and removal system of the city.
COUNTY: The county of Gooding, state of Idaho.
CUSTOMER: An occupant or owner of any premises in the city for which solid
waste service is, or has been, provided.
FRANCHISEE: Any person or entity authorized by the city of Hagerman, or
employed by the city of Hagerman to collect, handle, transport and dispose of
solid waste and/or recyclable materials and who has executed a franchise
agreement with the city of Hagerman.
HAZARDOUS MATERIALS: Any chemical, compound, mixture, substance or article
which is designated by the United States environmental protection agency or
appropriate agency of the state to be "hazardous", as that term is defined by
or pursuant to federal or state law.
INSPECTOR: The authorized employee or employees of the city of Hagerman, or
some individual designated by the city council as having the duty of
enforcement of this chapter.
MANDATORY: Every resident, business, entity or owner of a residential unit
within the city is required to use the collection and disposal system
established by the city.
OWNER: The person owning the real property where solid waste is created or
accumulated.
PERSON: Any individual, partnership, association, firm, corporation, public
agency, or any other legal entity.
PREMISES: Land and all buildings and structures thereon. "Premises" can be of
two (2) or more classifications, defined as:
Commercial Premises: Business, industrial, and institutional premises and
activities located within a commercially or industrially zoned district of the
city or operating with a valid issued special use permit in a residentially
zoned district, as distinct from residential or multi-family premises.
Multi-Family Premises: A dwelling or structure where more than one family
resides.
Residential Premises: A dwelling or structure where a person or group of
persons reside.
PROHIBITED WASTE: A. Includes any wastes that have any of the following general
characteristics:
        1. Extreme temperature;
        2. Harmful vapors;
        3. The presence of corrosive, flammable, explosive or toxic chemicals;
        4. Any materials with physical or other properties which render
collection operations hazardous; or
        5. Any materials which create a risk to the environment or public
health and safety.
   B.   In addition to wastes with the general characteristics described above,
prohibited wastes include:
      1. Liquid wastes, both bulk and contained;
        2. Tires;
        3. Any material regulated by the state of Idaho or the United States
environmental protection agency (40 CFR 260 through 268) as hazardous waste;
        4. Any equipment or machines containing refrigerants;
        5. Infectious wastes generated from business sources such as hospitals,
clinics, medical, surgical, dental, nursing homes, veterinarian offices, and
laboratories. Generators of infectious waste are required to sterilize,
package, or otherwise process the infectious waste so that it may be collected
without hazard to collection personnel and the general public; and
        6. Dead animal remains in an amount exceeding twenty five (25) pounds,
excluding animal carcasses if broken down and placed into plastic solid waste
bags and into a lidded, airtight and watertight container.
PUTRESCIBLE WASTE: Wastes that can decay and stink or become putrid.
RECYCLABLE MATERIALS: Products, including paper, cardboard, metal, glass, or
other substance capable of being reprocessed into consumer materials, which
have served the purpose for which they were originally manufactured or produced
and have passed through their end usage as consumer items, and which have been
discarded or placed for collection by their owner, whether or not such products
have monetary value.
REFUSE: All putrescible and nonputrescible solid waste (except sewage),
including garbage and rubbish.
RESIDENT: Every person, including lessees and occupants, in possession, charge,
custody, or control of any premises, residential or commercial, where solid
waste is created or accumulated.
RESIDENTIAL UNIT: A dwelling within the corporate limits of the city occupied
by a person or group of persons comprising not more than three (3) families. A
"residential unit" shall be deemed occupied when either water or domestic light
and power services are being supplied thereto. A condominium dwelling, whether
single or multi-level construction, consisting of three (3) or less continuous
or separate single-family dwelling units, shall be treated as a residential
unit, except that each single-family dwelling within any such residential unit
may be billed separately as a residential unit. Each separate rental unit, in
the case of a multi-family dwelling, shall be considered as a residential unit
and billed separately.
RUBBISH: All waste wood, wood products, tree trimmings, grass cuttings, dead
plants, weeds, leaves, dead trees or branches thereof, chips, shavings,
sawdust, printed matter, paper, pasteboard, rags, straw, used and discarded
mattresses, used and discarded shoes and boots, combustible waste, pulp and
other products such as are used for packaging, or wrapping crockery, and glass,
ashes, cinders, floor sweepings, glass, mineral or metallic substances, and any
and all other waste materials not included in the definition of "bulky waste",
"construction debris", dead animals, garbage, "hazardous materials" or "stable
matter".
SEWAGE: Water carried wastes from residences, commercial or industrial
establishments, business buildings, and other premises, containing polluted
matter subject to treatment at the sewage treatment plant.
SOLID WASTE: Any ashes, garbage, refuse, or rubbish, or any combination
thereof.
STABLE MATTER: All manure and other waste matter normally accumulated in or
about a stable, or any animal, livestock or poultry enclosure, and resulting
from the keeping of animals, poultry or livestock. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-3: MANDATORY SERVICE:
In order to maintain the public health, safety, and aesthetics of the city, all
owners and/or occupants of any residential units are required to pay for, and
are provided, solid waste collection services. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-4: COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL REQUIREMENTS; UNLAWFUL PRACTICES:
   A.   System Of Collection Established:
      1.   There is hereby established a system of solid waste collection,
transportation and disposal.
      2.   It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of
collecting, transporting, hauling, or conveying any solid waste, other than
from a commercial premises, over the streets or alleys of the city, or to dump
or dispose of the same, unless and until such person has a franchise, license,
or contract as an authorized representative of the city.
   B.   Compliance With Chapter Required: All refuse accumulated in the city
shall be collected, conveyed and disposed of as provided by this chapter, and
no person shall collect, or convey over any of the streets, alleys or public
ways in the city, or dispose of any refuse accumulated in the city except as
provided in this chapter.
   C.   Commercial Premises Exempt: The requirements under this section for the
collection and hauling of waste within the city shall not apply to commercial
premises.
   D.   Use Of System; Special Exception:
      1.   Every person who is an owner or occupant of premises within the city
limits shall use the refuse collection and disposal system herein provided and
shall deposit or cause to be disposed of in accordance with this chapter all
refuse which is accumulated on such premises; provided, that nothing herein is
to be construed to prohibit any owner from transporting and disposing of refuse
accumulated on his own premises, subject to all regulations herein contained.
      2.   An individual or entity may be granted a special exception from the
mandatory system used by the city council in extreme circumstances upon
application and a showing before the city council that the city, its licensee
or franchisee cannot reasonably accommodate the collection of the individual's
or entity's garbage. Upon being granted the exception, the garbage collector
must comply with the license, contract, and franchise provisions of this
chapter.
   E.   Lower Price Charged By Collector Not A Factor: The fact that another
garbage collector is willing to collect the garbage for a price less than the
price set by the city shall not be a factor in determining whether the city,
its licensee or franchisee can reasonably accommodate the collection of the
individual's or entity's garbage.
   F.   Minimum Payment Required: All owners or occupants of premises within
the city limits will be charged the minimum collection charge regardless of
whether they actually use the collection system provided by the city.
   G.   Refuse Accumulations Prohibited:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit, or to cause, the
accumulation in or about any premises or upon any street, alley or public way
of the city adjacent to such premises, owned or occupied by him, of garbage,
refuse and rubbish in an amount and/or manner as to constitute a health menace
or a nuisance.
      2.   It shall be unlawful to place, deposit or leave, or permit to
remain, anywhere in the city any garbage, rubbish or refuse except as provided
in this chapter.
      3.   It shall be unlawful to cause or permit to accumulate any garbage,
rubbish or refuse in such a manner that it can be blown away by the wind or
cause littering of public or private premises, streets, alleys and public ways
of the city.
   H.   Construction Dirt Or Debris: It shall be unlawful for any person to
deposit into the refuse system, dirt or earth debris from construction or
building renovation, rocks, stones, automobile bodies and parts, washing
machines, refrigerators, hot water tanks, stoves, tree trunks and stumps, and
other similar materials, dead animals, furniture, building materials such as
mortar, plaster, scrap lumber, broken concrete, and brick, waste oils and
lubricants from garages, service stations, machine shops, restaurants and other
similar establishments. Such material shall be collected and disposed of by the
building contractor, person, owner, occupant of the premises, or by the person
responsible for same. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005; amd. 2010 Code)
8-3-5: LICENSE, CONTRACT OR FRANCHISE:
   A.   City Authorized To Enter Into Franchise Agreement: The city may enter
into a license, contract, or franchise agreement with an individual or entity
to collect, transport, convey and dispose of garbage and refuse upon, on or
over the streets, alleys and public ways of the city. The mayor and city
council have the sole authority to select and approve all persons who shall
enter into a franchise or license agreement; contract to perform all services
pertaining to sanitary collection and disposal under the provisions of this
chapter; to establish reasonable fees for licenses; and may establish
reasonable rules and regulations governing the conduct and operation of such
licensee or contractor. All franchise holders shall be bound by and comply with
the provisions of this chapter wherever applicable, and shall comply with all
requirements set forth by the city council, and shall observe and faithfully
perform the conditions and provisions of the license and the ordinances, rules
and regulations of the city.
   B.   Residential Premises Service: Residential premises solid waste service
is provided to residents of Hagerman by the city.
   C.   Commercial Service: Commercial premises located within the city will
not be provided solid waste service by the city. Any commercial premises may
use the services of any contractor for the collection of solid waste within the
city limits without it being a violation of this chapter. However, no entity or
contractor may be allowed to collect from any residential premises in the city
without the proper license and/or franchise from the city.
   D.   Franchise Required To Collect: Collection of solid waste for
residential premises within the city limits without a valid franchise or
license agreement is a violation of this chapter subject to the penalties
contained in section
8-3-12 of this chapter. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-6: SANITARY CONTAINERS:
   A.   Container Requirements: Sanitary containers for residential premises or
for commercial premises shall be as set forth by the city council.
   B.   Use Of Containers: It shall be the duty of the resident or owner of any
premises at all times to keep, or cause to be kept, containers, as defined in
this chapter, and to deposit or cause to be deposited therein all solid waste,
except as otherwise herein provided.
   C.   Covers: All containers shall be: 1) equipped with close fitting covers;
or 2) securely tied; or 3) otherwise closed to prevent the contents to be blown
by the wind or otherwise littered.
   D.   Compacting Of Waste: Solid waste or recyclable materials shall not be
compacted in a container to the extent of obstructing free and easy removal
from the container.
   E.   Restraint Of Animals: Residents and owners shall restrain their animals
from spreading solid waste, or recyclable materials left for collection, or
from interfering with pick up personnel during collection. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-
2005)
8-3-7: PRECOLLECTION PRACTICES:
   A.   Draining Of Liquids: All solid waste, before being placed or deposited
in sanitary containers for collection, shall have drained from it all free
liquids and may be wrapped and placed in paper or plastic bags.
   B.   Tree Trimmings Bundled: Tree trimmings, hedge clippings and similar
materials shall be cut to a length not to exceed four feet (4') and securely
tied in bundles no more than two feet (2') in diameter before being deposited
in the can for collection.
   C.   Grass And Leaves: Grass clippings, leaves, and garden debris, except
sod, dirt, and rocks, may be placed in the collection can.
   D.   Removal Of Container From Pick Up Location: At other than commercial
and alley pick up, all containers shall be removed from the curb line of
streets and public ways within twenty four (24) hours. Unauthorized
accumulation of garbage, rubbish and refuse on any premises is hereby declared
to be a nuisance and thereby prohibited.
   E.   Taking Of Solid Waste Or Recyclables:
      1.   All trash and recyclable materials placed for collection shall be
owned by, and is the responsibility of, the customer until the time of
collection. At the time of collection, all trash and recyclable materials
become the property of the franchisee.
      2.   It is a violation of this chapter for any person to take, examine,
uncover, snoop in, separate, gather, collect or salvage materials deposited in
solid waste containers except with the express permission of the generator of
the solid waste.
   F.   Theft Of Collection Services:
      1.   It is a violation of this chapter for any person, except for the
owner, occupant, or invitee, to place or deposit any materials in or around a
solid waste receptacle provided for the use of a specific business or premises,
or in or around the can or container at a residence without permission from
such owner or occupant.
      2.   It is a violation of this chapter for any person to place solid
waste at any premises within the city limits that is not generated at that
commercial, residential, or multi- family premises.
   G.   Disposal Of Waste: It is a violation of this chapter for any person to
throw, discard or deposit any solid waste in or upon any street, alley,
sidewalk or vacant ground, or in or upon any canal, irrigation ditch, drainage
ditch or other watercourse. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-8: CURBSIDE OR ALLEY COLLECTION; FREQUENCY OF COLLECTION:
   A.   Placement Of Containers: All containers shall be placed for collection
outside of all buildings and shall be placed in the alley adjoining such
premises or other convenient place easily accessible by the collector; if no
alley is conveniently available, such receptacle may be placed on the street,
parking or sidewalk.
   B.   Handling Of Containers:
      1.   All containers shall be replaced upright where found. Containers and
lids shall not be placed or thrown on streets, alleys, highways, or on
adjoining property. The collector shall not permit receptacles to be thrown
from the truck to the pavement or parkway nor in any other way permit damage to
occur by rough or improper handling thereof.
      2.   Space, private ground, public streets, alleys, or ways about the
containers and the collection truck shall be left free from solid waste spilled
during collection. The collector shall be responsible for removal of such
spillage, but shall not be responsible for cleaning up conditions created by
the resident around such containers.
   C.   Frequency Of Collection:
      1.   Solid waste accumulated at residences shall be collected at least
once a week.
      2.   Solid waste accumulated at the premises of commercial and business
places shall be collected at least once each week, unless the city provides for
alternative collection on a special exception basis.
      3.   If residential or commercial users desire a greater frequency of
collection, such residential or commercial user may pay an additional fee, rate
or charge to be fixed and approved by the city.
      4.   The days for collection and permitted hours for collections shall be
set by the city council. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-9: RATES, FEES, CHARGES AND DEPOSITS:
   A.   Rates Set By City; Billing And Collection: The rates, fees or charges
for the collection and disposal of garbage and refuse shall at all times be
subject to the right of the city to prescribe and regulate the rates, fees and
charges made for services rendered or to be rendered. The city may bill and
collect all fees and charges.
   B.   Failure To Pay Bills: Failure to pay an account within fifteen (15)
days when due may subject the owner, tenant, lessee or occupant to withdrawal
or suspension of service as well as withdrawal or suspension of water and sewer
service, and such civil remedies provided by law.
   C.   Service Suspension; Deposit: In the event that garbage or water service
has been suspended or terminated by the city for nonpayment of fees, the city
shall, prior to reinstating said service, require an advance deposit equal to
three (3) months' projected service charge for said account.
   D.   Hauler May Collect Deposit: The city shall have the authority to
authorize its trash contract hauler to collect a deposit prior to delivery of
temporary box containers.
   E.   Special Fund Established: The proceeds from the collection of fees and
charges herein provided shall be placed in a special fund to be known as the
"solid waste collection account", and all expenses of the city in the operation
of the sanitary collection system shall be paid out of such fund, and any
surplus remaining therein at the end of each fiscal year may be transferred by
the council to the general fund. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-10: SOLID WASTE COLLECTION VEHICLES; INSPECTION:
   A.   Furnishing And Maintaining Trucks And Equipment: The contractor will
furnish a sufficient number of workers, trucks and equipment to collect and
dispose of solid wastes collected in the city. Said equipment shall be
maintained and operated in a clean and sanitary condition at the expense of the
contractor.
   B.   Specifications And Condition Of Vehicles: The contractor shall furnish
vehicles especially designed for the collection and hauling of solid waste and
waste products. All solid waste vehicles shall be closed and watertight, front,
rear, or side loading, commonly known as packers for collecting solid waste.
The equipment shall be clean, uniformly painted and marked and identified,
subject to review and approval by the city. All vehicles will be licensed,
lighted and safety inspected for highway operations.
   C.   Roadside Littering From Packer Vehicles: No roadside littering from
packer vehicles or from loading practices will be allowed. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-
2005)
8-3-11: SEPARATION AND RECYCLING:
The city reserves the right to, and may at its option, require the separation
of garbage, rubbish, or other components of solid waste, require the deposit
thereof in separate containers, and prescribe the method of disposal thereof.
The city also reserves the right to issue further regulations for the placement
and disposal of recyclable materials. The contractor shall cooperate at all
times with efforts to promote recycling of consumer products in the separation,
transportation, and deposit of identified recyclable materials. Any extra work
caused by said handling of recyclable materials over and above the contract
price will be the subject of prior separate contractual negotiations between
the city and the contractor. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005)
8-3-12: PENALTY FOR INFRACTION:
Any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company or
organization of any kind, including any owner, occupant, lessee or tenant of
premises, violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be deemed
guilty of an infraction and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to
penalty as provided in subsection
1-4-1B of this code. Each day such a violation is committed or permitted to
continue shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punishable as such
hereunder. (Ord. 1033, 9-21-2005; amd. 2010 Code)
TITLE 9
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING CODES AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-1-1: Codes Adopted; Building Permits And Fees
9-1-2: Area Of City Impact
9-1-1: CODES ADOPTED; BUILDING PERMITS AND FEES:
   A.   Purpose: The purpose of this section is to provide minimum standards
and requirements for regulating and controlling grading, quality, and
installation of materials, use occupancy, and maintenance of all buildings,
mobile homes, manufactured homes, and structures in the City of Hagerman.
Further, to bring the City of Hagerman ordinances into compliance with
requirements of the laws of the State of Idaho.
   B.   Adoption Of Applicable Codes:
      1.   The approved editions of the following codes, as adopted by the
State of Idaho and as required by Idaho Code 39-4116 and 39-4109, are adopted
as the official building codes of the City of Hagerman, State of Idaho, except
as provided in this section:
         a.   The 2012 version of the International Building Code; including
all rules promulgated by the board to provide the equivalency with the
provisions of the Americans With Disabilities Act accessibility guidelines and
the Federal Fair Housing Act accessibility guidelines, but not including the
other referenced codes in the International Building Code.
         b.   The International Residential Code, parts I - IV and IX.
         c.   The International Energy Conservation Code.
      2.   Provided that the adopted versions of these codes shall be
superseded by successive versions of these codes as they are adopted by the
Idaho Building Code Board pursuant to the statutes set forth above, and further
that these codes shall be effective upon the effective date as adopted by the
Idaho Building Code Board.
   C.   Building Permit Requirements: The following requirements must be met,
if applicable, prior to the issuance of a building permit:
      1.   Applicants shall provide plans and specifications of sufficient
detail to reflect compliance with Code requirements.
      2.   Applicants shall submit a completed building permit application with
the required supporting documentation.
      3.   Whenever any work for which a permit is required by this section
and/or the Building Code has been commenced without first obtaining the
required permit, a fee in addition to the regular permit fee shall be imposed;
with the additional fee to be set by the City of Hagerman in compliance with
this section.
   D.   Fees: The City of Hagerman shall establish fees for the issuance of all
required permits, including but not limited to building permits, plan reviews,
reinspections, and additional fees for commencing work prior to acquiring
permit. These fees shall be set by resolution by the City Council in such
amounts and at such times, as they may deem appropriate.
   E.   Violations: Violations of any provision of this section and/or failure
to comply with any of its requirements shall be a misdemeanor offense as
defined by Idaho Code. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. Each violation may be punished by imprisonment and up to six
(6) months and/or a fine of three hundred dollars ($300.00). The City may also
seek civil remedies to the maximum extent allowed by law. In addition, any
violation deemed by the City to threaten the public health, safety, and/or
general welfare of the City, the City Council may take any lawful action they
deem necessary to abate such violation. (Ord. 1062, 3-5-2014)
9-1-2: AREA OF CITY IMPACT:
   A.   Facility For Commercial Propagation Of Fish Unlawful: Notwithstanding
any provision of the international building code or any other section of this
code, no permit shall be granted for the construction or maintenance of a
facility for the commercial propagation of fish within the impact area of the
city. The construction or maintenance of a facility for the commercial
propagation of fish is unlawful.
   B.   Building Code Enforcement: All regulations, provisions, penalties and
conditions of said international building code shall apply and be enforced by
the city in the area of city impact as described in ordinance 933 of the city
of Hagerman and as described in ordinance 20 of the ordinances of Gooding
County, or as said area may hereafter be fixed and described 1 . (1996 Code §
3-1-2; amd. Ord. 1017, 12-17-2002)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 1, chapter 8 of this code.
CHAPTER 2
FIRE PREVENTION CODES AND REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-2-1: Fire Codes Adopted
9-2-2: LP Gas And Fuel Oil Tank Regulations
9-2-1: FIRE CODES ADOPTED:
   A.   Adoption: The following are hereby adopted by the city for the purpose
of prescribing regulations regarding conditions hazardous to life and property
from fire or explosions: 1) that certain code and standard known as the
international fire code, including appendices; and 2) the international fire
code standards published by the Western Fire Chiefs Association and the
International Conference Of Building Officials, being particularly the latest
editions thereof. One copy of the code and standard has been and now is filed
with the city clerk-treasurer, and the same is hereby adopted and incorporated
as fully as if set forth at length herein, and from the effective date hereof,
the provisions thereof shall be controlling within the limits of the city.
(Ord. 1021, 9-2-2003)
   B.   Definitions: Wherever the following terms are used in the fire codes
adopted in subsection A of this section, the meanings thereof shall be as
follows:
BUREAU OF FIRE PREVENTION: This term is referring to the fire chief of the fire
district or his designee.
JURISDICTION: The city of Hagerman area of impact. (1996 Code §
5-1-2; amd. 2010 Code)
   C.   Appeal: Whenever the chief disapproves an application or refuses to
grant a permit applied for, or when it is claimed that the provisions of the
codes adopted in subsection A of this section do not apply or that the true
intent of the meaning of said codes has been misconstrued or wrongly
interpreted, the applicant may appeal from the decision of the chief of the
fire district to the city council within thirty (30) days from the date of the
decision appealed. (1996 Code §
5-1-3)
   D.   Violations; Penalties:
      1.   Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of the code or
standards adopted in subsection A of this section, or fails to comply
therewith, or who shall violate or fail to comply with any order made
hereunder, or who shall build in violation of any detailed statement of
specifications or plans submitted and approved thereunder, or any certificate
or permit issued thereunder, and from which no appeal has been taken, or who
shall fail to comply with such an order as affirmed or modified by the fire
chief of the fire district or by a court of competent jurisdiction, within the
time fixed herein, shall severally for each and every such violation and
noncompliance, be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1996 Code §
5-1-4; amd. 2010 Code)
      2.   The imposition of one penalty for any violation shall not excuse the
violation or permit it to continue; and all such persons shall be required to
correct or remedy such violation or defects within a reasonable time; and when
not otherwise specified, each ten (10) days that prohibited conditions are
maintained shall constitute a separate offense.
      3.   The application of the above penalties shall not be held to prevent
the enforced removal of prohibited conditions. (1996 Code §
5-1-4)
9-2-2: LP GAS AND FUEL OIL TANK REGULATIONS:
   A.   LP Gas Tank Sizes:
      1.   Residential zone: Two hundred fifty (250) gallon. If larger quantity
is needed, additional tanks must be installed as outlined in the international
fire code.
      2.   Commercial zone: Five hundred (500) gallon.
      3.   Industrial zone: Tanks larger than five hundred (500) gallon must be
placed in the industrial area.
      4.   All tanks must be installed according to the regulations set forth
in the international fire code.
   B.   Fuel Oil Tank Sizes:
      1.   Tank size shall be no greater than three hundred sixty (360) gallon.
      2.   All tanks must be installed according to the regulations set forth
in the international fire code.
   C.   New Installations; Notify Fire District: The building inspector for the
city must contact the Hagerman fire district whenever LP gas or fuel oil is
being installed in new construction. (Ord. 1021, 9-2-2003; amd. 2010 Code)
CHAPTER 3
UNSAFE BUILDINGS OR STRUCTURES
SECTION:
9-3-1: Buildings Or Structures Declared Unsafe
9-3-2: Public Nuisance
9-3-3: Procedures For Abatement
9-3-1: BUILDINGS OR STRUCTURES DECLARED UNSAFE:
Buildings, structures or attachments which are structurally unsafe or which
constitute a fire hazard or are otherwise dangerous to human life are, for
purposes of this chapter, unsafe. (Ord. 1009, 3-22-2000)
9-3-2: PUBLIC NUISANCE:
All unsafe buildings, structures or attachments are hereby declared to be a
public nuisance and shall be abated by repair, rehabilitation or demolition or
removal in accordance with procedures set forth herein. (Ord. 1009, 3-22-2000)
9-3-3: PROCEDURES FOR ABATEMENT 1 :
   A.   Declaration As Unsafe; Notice:
      1.   The building inspector shall make the initial determination whether
any building, structure or attachment is a public nuisance and possesses a
threat to the public safety or welfare.
      2.   Upon a determination that a building, structure or attachment is a
public nuisance, the building inspector shall give the owner and/or occupant of
the building verbal notification of the determination. The building inspector
shall also serve written notice by personal service or certified mail to the
owner and/or occupant of the property within twenty four (24) hours of his
determination. The notification shall set forth the building inspector's
findings and what steps can be taken to abate the nuisance. A copy of the
written notice shall be given to the city clerk- treasurer.
   B.   Posting Notices On Property: The building inspector shall post all
appropriate notices on the property and take the appropriate steps to protect
the public safety and welfare.
   C.   Notice Of Public Hearing: Upon receipt of the written notice from the
building inspector, the city clerk-treasurer shall schedule a hearing before
the city council at the next regular or special meeting of the city council, to
determine if the building, structure or attachment is a public nuisance. Notice
of the hearing shall be served upon the owner and occupant of the property by
the city police and/or mailed to the owner and occupant of the property. The
clerk- treasurer shall place the hearing upon the agenda for the next meeting.
   D.   Hearing; Presentation Of Evidence; Council Decision:
      1.   At the hearing before the council, the building inspector shall
present evidence of the public nuisance to the council. The owner of the
property shall be allowed to present such evidence or testimony to the council
as the owner chooses.
      2.   The council shall make its decision on declaring the property a
public nuisance and give the owner a copy of the decision and what actions the
owner can take to cure the nuisance. (Ord. 1009, 3-22-2000; amd. 2010 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  4-1-8 of this code.
CHAPTER 4
HISTORIC PRESERVATION
SECTION:
9-4-1: Purpose
9-4-2: Definitions
9-4-3: Historic Preservation Commission Established
9-4-4: Organization; Officers; Rules; Meetings
9-4-5: Powers, Duties And Responsibilities
9-4-6: Special Restrictions
9-4-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to promote the educational, cultural, economic
and general welfare of the public of the city through the identification,
evaluation, designation, and protection of those buildings, sites, areas,
structures, and objects which reflect significant elements of the city's, the
state's, and the nation's historic, architectural, archaeological, and cultural
heritage. (Ord. 958, 9-16-1986)
9-4-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have, unless
the context clearly indicates otherwise, the following meanings:
CITY: The city of Hagerman.
COMMISSION: The historic preservation commission of the city of Hagerman.
HISTORIC PRESERVATION: The research, documentation, protection, restoration and
rehabilitation of buildings, structures, objects, districts, areas, and sites
significant in the history, architecture, archaeology or culture of this state,
its communities or the nation.
HISTORIC PROPERTY: Any building, structure, area or site that is significant in
the history, architecture, archaeology or culture of this community, the state,
or the nation. (1996 Code § 4-6-1)
9-4-3: HISTORIC PRESERVATION COMMISSION ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Commission Established: There is hereby created a historic preservation
commission that shall consist of five (5) members who shall be appointed by the
mayor with the advice and consent of the city council.
   B.   Membership: All members of the commission shall have a demonstrated
interest, competence, or knowledge in history or historic preservation. The
council shall endeavor to appoint at least two (2) members with professional
training or experience in the disciplines of architecture, history,
architectural history, urban planning, archaeology, engineering, law, or other
historic preservation related disciplines.
   C.   Initial Appointments; Filling Vacancies:
      1.   Initial appointments to the commission shall be made as follows: one
1-year term; two (2) 2-year terms; two (2) 3-year terms. All subsequent
appointments shall be made for three (3) year terms.
      2.   Vacancies shall be filled in the same manner as original
appointments and the appointee shall serve for the remainder of the unexpired
term. (1996 Code § 4-6-2)
9-4-4: ORGANIZATION; OFFICERS; RULES; MEETINGS:
   A.   Rules And Bylaws: The commission shall have the power to make whatever
rules are necessary for the execution of its duties as set forth in this
chapter. Rules of procedure and bylaws adopted by the commission shall be
available for public inspection.
   B.   Officers: The commission shall elect officers from among the commission
members. The chairman shall preside at meetings of the commission. The vice
chairman shall, in the absence of the chairman, perform the duties of the
chairman.
   C.   Open Meetings: All meetings of the commission shall be open to the
public, and follow the requirements of the Idaho open meeting law 1 . The
commission shall keep minutes and other appropriate written records of its
resolutions, proceedings, and actions.
   D.   Recommend Employment Or Contracting: The commission may recommend to
the council, within the limits of its funding, the employment of or the
contracting with other parties for the service of technical experts or other
persons as it deems necessary to carry on the functions of the commission.
(1996 Code § 4-6-3)
 
Notes
1 1. IC § 67-2341 et seq.
9-4-5: POWERS, DUTIES AND RESPONSIBILITIES:
The commission shall be advisory to the council and shall be authorized to:
   A.   Conduct a survey of local historic properties.
   B.   Recommend the acquisition of fee and lesser interests in historic
properties, including adjacent or associated lands, by purchase, bequests, or
donations.
   C.   Recommend methods and procedures necessary to preserve, restore,
maintain and operate historic properties under the ownership or control of the
city.
   D.   Recommend the lease, sale, or other transfer or disposition of historic
properties subject to rights of public access and other covenants and in a
manner that will preserve the property.
   E.   Contract, with the approval of the council, with the state or federal
government, or any agency of either, or with any other organization.
   F.   Cooperate with the federal, state, and local governments in the
pursuance of the objectives of historic preservation.
   G.   Make recommendations in the planning processes undertaken by the
county, the city, the state, or the federal government and the agencies of
these entities.
   H.   Recommend ordinances and otherwise provide information for the purpose
of historic preservation in the city.
   I.   Promote and conduct an educational and interpretive program on historic
preservation and historic properties in the city.
   J.   Commission members, employees or agents of the commission may enter
private property, buildings, or structures in the performance of their official
duties only with the express consent of the owner or occupant thereof.
   K.   Review nominations of properties to the national register of historic
places for properties within the city's jurisdiction. (1996 Code § 4-6-4)
9-4-6: SPECIAL RESTRICTIONS:
Under the provisions of Idaho Code section 67-4612, the city may provide, by
ordinances, special conditions or restrictions for the protection, enhancement
and preservation of historic properties. (1996 Code § 4-6-5)
CHAPTER 5
MANUFACTURED HOMES AND MANUFACTURED HOME PARKS 1
SECTION:
9-5-1: Definitions
9-5-2: Organization And Enforcement
9-5-3: Manufactured Homes Outside Manufactured Home Park
9-5-4: Permit Requirements
9-5-5: Mobile/Manufactured Home Park Requirements
9-5-6: Unsafe Conditions
9-5-7: Nonconforming Uses
9-5-8: Access To Public Street
9-5-9: Access And Inspection
9-5-10: Violation; Penalty
 
Notes
  1. See also "manufactured homes" in section
1 10-4A-2, and sections
  11-6-5 and
  11-6-6 of this code.
9-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have the
meanings ascribed to them in this section:
APPROVED: Approval by the building inspector as the result of investigation for
compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
BUILDING: Any structure built for the support, shelter or enclosure of persons,
animals, chattels or property of any kind.
GRADE: The average of the finished ground level of the premises.
INSPECTOR: The building inspector or any legally designated representative of
the city.
MANUFACTURED HOME: A structure constructed according to HUD/FHA mobile home
construction and safety standards, transportable in one or more sections,
which, in the traveling mode, is eight (8) body feet or more in width or is
forty (40) body feet or more in length, and when erected on site is one
thousand (1,000) square feet or more in size, and which is built on a permanent
chassis, and designed to be used as a dwelling unit with a permanent foundation
when connected to the required utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating,
air conditioning and electrical systems contained therein. Manufactured homes
shall not include travel trailers, or other similar recreational vehicles, and
shall not include manufactured homes or mobile homes constructed prior to the
year of the adoption of this title.
MOBILE HOME: All vehicles used, or so constructed as to permit being conveyed
upon the public streets or highways as such and constructed in such a manner as
will permit occupancy thereof for human habitation, constructed prior to 1976.
MOBILE/MANUFACTURED HOME PARK: Any area, tract, plot, or site of land whereupon
mobile homes, as defined in this chapter, are placed, located and maintained
for dwelling purposes only, either on a permanent or semipermanent basis and
for which a fee, rental or contract for payment for such use is collected or
collectible to the person holding the land.
MOBILE/MANUFACTURED HOME SPACE: A plot of ground within a mobile home park, or
any plot of ground that is designed for or designated as the location for a
mobile home and manufactured home.
MOBILE STRUCTURES: All vehicles designed for human habitation.
OFFICIAL: A person who has either been duly elected or appointed to a public
office and who represents the city government for a prescribed duty or
capacity.
PERMITTEE: Any individual, firm, trust, partnership, association or
corporation, whether tenant, owner, lessee, licensee, permittee, agency, heirs
or assigns.
PERSON: Any individual, firm, trust, partnership, association or corporation,
whether tenant, owner, lessee, licensee, permittee, agency, heirs or assigns.
STRUCTURE: That which is built or constructed, an edifice or building of any
kind, or any piece or work artificially built up or composed of parts joined in
some definite manner.
TRAILER: See definition of Mobile Home.
YARD: An open space within a lot unoccupied and unobstructed from the ground
upward. (1996 Code § 4-5-1; amd. 2010 Code)
9-5-2: ORGANIZATION AND ENFORCEMENT:
The building inspector of the city or his duly authorized representative shall
be charged with the enforcement of this chapter and shall keep a permanent,
accurate account of all fees and other monies collected, the amount, purpose
and person from whom it was received, together with the location of the
premises to which they relate. (1996 Code § 4-5-14)
9-5-3: MANUFACTURED HOMES OUTSIDE MANUFACTURED HOME PARK:
   A.   Location: Manufactured homes not located within a mobile home park must
be located on a legal city lot.
   B.   Age Of Manufactured Home; Inspection: Each manufactured home must have
been manufactured after the year 1976, and may not be occupied until approved
by the building inspector.
   C.   Manufactured Home Requirements: Each manufactured home not in a
manufactured home park must meet the following requirements:
      1.   The manufactured home shall be placed on an excavated and backfilled
foundation and enclosed at the perimeter such that the home is located not more
than twelve inches (12") above grade.
      2.   The manufactured home shall have a pitched roof, except that no
standards shall require a slope of greater than a nominal three feet (3') in
height for each twelve feet (12') in width.
      3.   The manufactured home shall have exterior siding and roofing which
in color, material and appearance is similar to the exterior siding and roofing
material commonly used on residential dwellings within the community or which
is comparable to the predominant materials used on surrounding dwellings, as
determined by the local permit approval authority.
      4.   If the manufactured home has a garage or carport, such garage shall
be constructed of like material.
   D.   Number Of Homes On Lot: It shall be unlawful for any person to maintain
two (2) or more occupied mobile/manufactured homes on a single legal building
site, other than in a manufactured home park.
   E.   Replacement; Permit Required: Replacement of an existing mobile/
manufactured home due to fire, etc., shall not be without a permit. (1996 Code
§ 4-5-2)
9-5-4: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Permits Required; Fee:
      1.   It is unlawful for any person to build, establish, maintain, operate
or permit to be built, established, maintained or operated, any recreational
vehicle park or manufactured home park within the bounds of the city without
first having secured all proper zoning and building permits. Pre-1976 mobile
homes shall not be accepted, unless already on site prior to July 1995. (1996
Code § 4-5-3)
      2.   The permit fee for each manufactured home park shall be set by
resolution. (1996 Code § 4-5-10)
   B.   Application For Permit: To obtain a permit for the construction or
alteration of a manufactured home park or the placement of a manufactured home
outside a manufactured home park, the applicant shall:
      1.   Identify and describe the work to be covered by the permit for which
the application is made.
      2.   Describe the land on which the proposed work is to be done by legal
description, street address and physical location.
      3.   Show the use and occupancy for such lot, block and tract.
      4.   State the true valuation of the proposed improvements.
      5.   Be signed by the permittee or his authorized agent.
      6.   Give such other information as may reasonably be required by the
building inspector. (1996 Code § 4-5-4)
   C.   Issuance Of Permit; Compliance With Requirements: The application with
a sketch will be filed by the applicant for a permit. If the building inspector
is satisfied that the proposal, as submitted, subject to corrections, meets the
requirements as set forth in this chapter, he shall then issue the permit
therefor to the applicant. The septic system must be installed and approved by
the Central health district. (1996 Code § 4-5-5)
   D.   Retention Of Plans: One set of approved plans, specifications and
computations shall be retained by the building inspector for a period of not
less than one hundred eighty (180) days from date of completion of the work
covered therein, and one set of approved plans and specifications shall be
returned to the applicant, which set shall be kept on such building or work
during the time the work authorized thereby is in progress. (1996 Code § 4-5-6)
   E.   Validity Of Permit: The issuance or granting of a permit or approval of
plans and specifications shall not be construed to be a permit for, or an
approval of, any violation of any of the provisions of this chapter. (1996 Code
§ 4-5-7)
   F.   Expiration Of Permit: Every permit issued by the building inspector
under the provisions of this chapter shall expire by limitation and become null
and void, if the building or work authorized by such permit is not commenced
within one hundred eighty (180) days from the date of such permit. Also, such
permit shall become null and void if the building or work authorized by such
permit is suspended or abandoned for a period of one hundred eighty (180) days
any time after the work is commenced. (1996 Code § 4-5-8)
   G.   Inspections: All construction or work for which a permit is required
shall be subject to inspection by the building inspector. (1996 Code § 4-5-11)
   H.   Suspension Or Revocation Of Permit: The building inspector may, in
writing, suspend or revoke a permit issued under provisions of this chapter
whenever the permit is issued on the basis of incorrect information supplied,
or in violation of any ordinance or regulations or any of the provisions of
this chapter. (1996 Code § 4-5-9)
9-5-5: MOBILE/MANUFACTURED HOME PARK REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Density For Mobile Home Parks: In no event shall the density exceed
eight (8) mobile homes per gross acre. Density requirements shall be
established as the minimum square footage or gross site area for each mobile
home. If it is determined by the city council that a street widening or
terminating dedication is necessary, the amount of land dedicated shall be
subtracted from the gross site area when calculating the proposed density.
   B.   Application To Existing Homes And Mobile Home Parks: A mobile home, a
manufactured home and a mobile home park, lawfully existing and in use at the
effective date hereof may be continued although such mobile home park, mobile
home or manufactured home may not conform to the provisions of this chapter as
herein set forth.
   C.   Manufactured Home Parks:
      1.   Abandoning Standards; Council Approval Required: Every manufactured
or mobile home park that conforms to any of the standards listed below shall
not abandon any of the standards listed below without obtaining approval from
the city council.
      2.   Central Facilities: Central facilities such as toilets, baths, or
laundry rooms are not required.
      3.   Streets And Roads:
         a.   All spaces shall abut upon a roadway not less than twenty feet
(20') in width which shall have unobstructed access to a public street or
highway, as set forth in the city subdivision ordinance. Dead end roadways
shall provide adequate vehicle turning space or cul-de-sac with not less than a
sixty foot (60') radius exclusive of parking. Roads to service areas or storage
yards shall be not less than twenty feet (20') wide.
         b.   Directory and regulatory signs shall be provided as required to
assure maximum safety and convenience to occupants and visitors, consistent
with accepted safety standards.
      4.   Minimum Requirements: Each manufactured home space shall be not less
than forty feet (40') wide and one hundred feet (100') long.
      5.   Increase In Number Of Spaces: Any manufactured home park existing at
the effective date hereof that increases the number of manufactured home spaces
must bring the entire manufactured home park up to the specifications contained
in this section.
      6.   Other Requirements: All such parks shall conform to the following
requirements:
         a.   Shall be located on a well drained site with all roadways and
spaces properly graded to ensure rapid drainage and freedom from stagnant pools
of water;
         b.   All roadways and walks within a recreational vehicle or
manufactured home park shall be all weather surfaced, maintained and adequately
lighted. (1996 Code § 4-5-12)
   D.   Water Supply:
      1.   The park shall connect to the city water system. The water supply
shall be easily accessible to each manufactured home space, shall provide not
less than twenty five (25) pounds of pressure at all times and not less than
one hundred twenty five (125) gallons per unit per day. All water supplies must
be approved by the public works superintendent.
      2.   Manufactured home parks shall meet existing state fire code
regulations.
   E.   Plumbing: All plumbing shall be within the standards set forth in the
international building code and shall be subject to inspection and approval by
the designated officials. (1996 Code § 4-5-12; amd. 2010 Code)
   F.   Sewage Disposal: All sewage shall be collected and disposed of in a
sanitary manner, either in a public sewage system or in conformance with
standards set forth in the state health district.
   G.   Electricity: All installations of electrical wiring and equipment in
recreational vehicle and manufactured home parks shall conform to the minimum
requirements of the state.
   H.   Yard Requirements:
      1.   Manufactured home parks shall set back at least ten feet (10') from
any interior property line. The setback from any abutting public street shall
be at least twenty feet (20') from the properly line.
      2.   In any required yard through which automobile access is taken
between a public or private parking area and a street, no fence, wall, hedge or
other vegetation shall be permitted which materially impedes vision from a
public sidewalk to automobiles backing from said parking area(s) across said
public sidewalk.
   I.   Parking Requirements:
      1.   There shall be one vehicle parking space at least nine feet by
twenty feet (9' x 20') in size for each manufactured home space, with clear and
unobstructed access to an accessway. Any parking in the accessway shall not
fulfill this requirement.
      2.   Guest parking shall be provided on the manufactured home parking
site (but not in the accessway) at the rate of one vehicle parking space of the
dimensions set forth in subsection I1 of this section for each manufactured
home space.
   J.   Skirting And Support Structure:
      1.   All manufactured homes shall be set on a permanent foundation and
shall have compatible skirting of moisture resistant, noncombustible material
or fire retardant wood, which must be maintained and not provide a harborage
for rodents.
      2.   All spaces shall be provided with pedestals or blocking supports.
Such systems shall ensure adequate support and be in compliance with the HUD
and manufacturer's specifications as to setup procedures and conform to city
building regulations 1 . (1996 Code § 4-5-12)
 
Notes
1 1. See chapter 1 of this title.
9-5-6: UNSAFE CONDITIONS:
All manufactured home parks, mobile homes and manufactured homes, buildings or
premises which constitute a hazard to health, safety, or fire by reason of
inadequate maintenance, insanitation, dilapidation, obsolescence or abandonment
are nuisances and shall be abated by repair, rehabilitation, demolition, or
removal, according to state laws. (1996 Code § 4-5-13)
9-5-7: NONCONFORMING USES:
   A.   A nonconforming use is a use existing at the effective date hereof or
of any earlier land use ordinance that is not permitted by provisions of this
chapter or the land use ordinance.
   B.   A nonconforming use may not be expanded in regard to actual land use or
in regard to building space used, except through an appropriate conditional use
permit. A nonconforming use may not be changed to another nonconforming use
without compliance with the terms of this title. (1996 Code § 4-5-15)
9-5-8: ACCESS TO PUBLIC STREET:
A manufactured home park, mobile home or manufactured home shall not be
established on any site that does not have access to a public street with less
than fifty feet (50') of right of way. No manufactured home space or
manufactured home shall be located in such a manner that a public street must
be used to maneuver the manufactured home into that space. (1996 Code § 4-5-16)
9-5-9: ACCESS AND INSPECTION:
   A.   Occupant And Owner: It shall be the duty of every occupant to give the
park owner or his agent access, at reasonable times, to any part of the park or
its premises for the purpose of making such repairs or alterations as are
necessary to effectuate compliance with this chapter, or any lawful order
issued.
   B.   Owners And City: It shall be the duty of the owners or occupants of
manufactured home parks and mobile homes and manufactured homes contained
therein, or of the person in charge thereof, to give the building inspector and
the city council or their duly authorized assistants free access to such
premises, upon notice to the management, at reasonable times, for the purpose
of inspection.
   C.   City Inspection: The building inspector and city council or their duly
authorized assistants are authorized and directed to inspect and determine the
condition of manufactured home parks, mobile homes and manufactured homes
within the city, in the performance of their duty to enforce the provisions of
this chapter and other applicable ordinances. (1996 Code § 4-5-17)
9-5-10: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
   A.   Any person who wilfully violates any provision of this chapter or who
wilfully violates any provision of the codes enumerated herein, is guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to penalty as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1996 Code § 4-5-18; amd. 2010 Code)
   B.   A separate violation is deemed to have occurred with respect to each
building not in compliance with this chapter. Each day such violation continues
constitutes a separate offense. (1996 Code § 4-5-18)
CHAPTER 6
SIGNS
SECTION:
9-6-1: Scope
9-6-2: Definitions
9-6-3: Sign Requirements
9-6-4: Manner Of Construction
9-6-5: Sandwich Board Signs
9-6-6: Banner Signs
9-6-1: SCOPE:
Sign regulations in the commercial and industrial areas will be permitted under
the rules set out in this chapter. (2010 Code)
9-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
BANNER SIGNS: A sign that is temporary, having characters, letters, or
illustrations applied to plastic, cloth, canvas, or other similar material,
with the purpose of such nonrigid material being for background.
FREESTANDING SIGN: A sign that is supported by one or more columns, upright
pole or brace extended from the ground or from an object on the ground, or that
is erected on the ground where no part of the sign is attached to any part of a
building, structure, or other sign; the term includes a "pole sign", "pedestal
sign", and "ground sign".
MARQUEE SIGN: A sign depicted upon, attached to, or supported by a marquee.
PROJECTING SIGN: A sign attached to a building or extending in whole or in part
fifteen inches (15") or more horizontally beyond the surface of the building to
which the sign is attached or suspended from a canopy.
ROOF SIGN: A sign supported by poles, uprights, or braces extending from the
roof of a building, or projecting above the roof of a building.
SANDWICH BOARD SIGN: A temporary sign that is generally constructed in such a
manner as to form an "A" or a tentlike shape that is placed on, but not
permanently attached to the ground. This definition also includes signs of
similar temporary nature but that are constructed with a base and a single
upward sign face, forming an upside down "T".
SIGN: Any device, fixture, placard, or structure that uses any color, form,
graphic, illumination, symbol, or writing to advertise, announce the purpose
of, or identify the purpose of a person or entity, or to communicate
information of any kind to the public.
SIGN, ILLUMINATED: Any sign illuminated by electricity, gas, or other
artificial light including reflecting or phosphorescent light.
SIGN, LIGHTING DEVICE: Any light, string of lights, or group of lights located
or arranged so as to cast illumination on a sign.
SIGN, OFF PREMISES: Any sign, including, without limitation, a billboard or
general outdoor advertising device, that advertises or directs attention to a
business, commodity, service, or activity conducted, sold, or offered other
than on the same lot or within the same building upon which such sign is
located.
SIGN, ON PREMISES: Any sign related to a business or profession conducted, or a
commodity or service sold or offered upon the premises, where such sign is
located.
WALL SIGN: A sign displayed upon or against the wall of an enclosed building,
where the exposed face of the sign is in place parallel to the plane of the
wall and extends not more than fifteen inches (15") horizontally from the face
of the wall.
WINDOW SIGN: A sign that is painted on, applied or attached to, or located
within one foot (1') from the window and can be seen from the exterior of the
structure, but excludes merchandise included in a window display. (2010 Code)
9-6-3: SIGN REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Projecting Signs:
      1.   Projecting signs are limited to one per business where such sign is
located.
      2.   The maximum size shall not exceed fifty (50) square feet per face or
one hundred (100) square feet per sign.
      3.   No point on any sign shall project more than ten feet (10') above
the highest point of the roof structure of the building to which it is
attached. Any sign exceeding four feet (4') in height shall provide a clearance
of not less than four feet (4') between the roof and the lowest point on the
sign. Signs attached to parapet walls shall not project more than six feet (6')
above the highest point of said parapet wall. Projecting signs and marquees
shall not project more than eight feet (8') from the principal building.
   B.   Freestanding Signs:
      1.   Freestanding signs are limited to the same size as projecting signs
with a maximum height of twenty feet (20').
      2.   No freestanding sign shall be set nearer to a lot line adjacent to a
street than the required minimum setback for the principal building.
   C.   Illuminated Signs:
      1.   Any illuminated sign or lighted device shall emit a light of
constant intensity, and no sign shall be illuminated by or contain flashing,
intermittent, rotating, or moving light or lights.
      2.   In no event shall an illuminated sign or lighting device be placed
or directed to permit the beams and illumination therefrom to be directed or
beamed onto a public thoroughfare, highway, sidewalk, or adjacent premises or
cause a glare or reflection that may constitute a traffic hazard or nuisance.
   D.   Signs With Moving Parts: No sign shall employ any parts or elements
which revolve, rotate, whirl, spin, or otherwise use motion to attract
attention (not to include any sign performing a public information service
function such as indicating time, temperature, stock market quotations or
similar services).
   E.   Signs Along Primary Highways: Signs along primary highways shall
conform to the state transportation department regulations. No sign shall be
placed in any public right of way except publicly owned signs. (2010 Code)
9-6-4: MANNER OF CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Wall Mounted Signs: All signs shall be supported from the buildings in
front of which they are placed with proper metal supports securely bolted or
fastened to the walls. All signs extending over the sidewalk shall be laterally
secured with guywires which are made adjustable by means of turnbuckles.
   B.   Freestanding Signs: Where buildings set back off of the property line,
signs shall be mounted on a single or double rigid pole that is securely
anchored in concrete, and placed on a line that is two feet (2') within the
curb line. No sign shall extend beyond a point two feet (2') within the curb
line and minimum vertical clearance shall be nine feet (9').
   C.   Rooftop Mounted Signs: The framework of all signs placed upon the roof
of any building or structure shall be so constructed and fastened to the roof
as to be capable of withstanding a wind pressure of not less than twenty (20)
pounds per square foot of surface area. Said sign shall be set back from the
firewall of said building or structure a distance of at least three feet (3')
so as to leave a clear passageway around and in front of the same. The bottom
line of the surface of said sign shall be at least four feet (4') in the clear
above the roof of said building so as to leave a clear passageway under the
same. (2010 Code)
9-6-5: SANDWICH BOARD SIGNS:
   A.   Definition: A "sandwich board sign" is a temporary sign that is
generally constructed in such a manner as to form an "A" or a tentlike shape
that is placed on, but not permanently attached to the ground. This definition
also includes signs of a similar temporary nature that are constructed with a
base and a single upward sign face, forming an upside down "T".
   B.   Conditions: Sandwich board signs are permissible subject to the
following conditions:
      1.   Temporary Display:
         a.   A sandwich board sign is considered a temporary sign and as such
can advertise a special sale for a maximum of thirty (30) days and must include
dates.
         b.   Sandwich board signs may be placed on properties during business
hours only and must be taken in at the end of business.
      2.   Placement:
         a.   Sandwich board signs shall not be located within a landscaped
area, parking space, or vehicular travelway.
         b.   Sandwich board signs shall not be located more than ten feet
(10') from the door of the business or use utilizing the sign.
         c.   A maximum of one sandwich board sign may be placed per business
or tenant on the property where the sandwich board sign(s) is located and be
properly secured.
         d.   Sandwich board signs shall be placed no closer than twenty feet
(20') from other sandwich board signs.
         e.   Sandwich board signs shall be located on the interior of the
property and shall not be located within any public right of way and/or
sidewalk.
         f.   Should a sandwich board sign be placed adjacent to a sidewalk, an
unobstructed pedestrian clearance must be provided adjacent to the sign.
      3.   Appearance And Maintenance:
         a.   The maximum size of a sandwich board sign is twelve (12) square
feet with a maximum height of four feet (4') and a maximum width of three feet
(3').
         b.   All signs shall be maintained with fresh paint or lettering and
not be left unkempt. All signs shall look neat and professional with an
artistic appearance. (2010 Code)
9-6-6: BANNER SIGNS:
   A.   Definition: A "banner sign" is a temporary sign having characters,
letters, or illustrations applied to plastic, cloth, canvas, or other similar
material, with the purpose of such nonrigid material being for background.
   B.   Conditions: Banner signs are permissible subject to the following
conditions:
      1.   Permit Required; Exception; Duration Of Display:
         a.   A sign permit shall be necessary to erect or place a banner sign
across State Highway 30 or on a property.
         b.   A sign permit shall not be issued to erect or place a banner sign
across State Highway 30 or on a property until a site plan has been approved by
the city.
         c.   Each banner sign must be permitted individually. Individual
banner signs can be placed for a maximum of five (5) weeks; four (4) weeks
prior to event and taken down no later than one week after event.
         d.   Arrangements for installation and removal of banner signs across
State Highway 30 must be made in advance by the group or organization using the
banner. Arrangements must be presented to the city in order to receive a sign
permit.
      2.   Placement:
         a.   Banner signs are allowed on a property in any area that does not
obstruct the view of intersections or driveways. Banner signs are not allowed
on rights of way.
         b.   With permission, banner signs may also be allowed during social
or athletic events at Coltharp Park or other city owned property. The banner
signs can be attached to the gazebo, fences, stakes, or poles for a maximum of
five (5) weeks; four (4) weeks prior to event and taken down no later than one
week after event.
      3.   Appearance And Maintenance:
         a.   All banner signs shall be maintained with fresh paint or
lettering and not be left unkempt. All signs shall look neat and professional
with an artistic appearance.
         b.   A banner sign shall be securely attached at all times. Banner
signs must be in good repair, taut, and vertical at all times with a sufficient
number of holes to allow for airflow in the event of wind. (2010 Code)
TITLE 10
ZONING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS, ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
10-1-1: Purposes
10-1-2: Declaration
10-1-3: Interpretation And Intent
10-1-4: Zoning Permit
10-1-5: Schedule Of Fees, Charges And Expenses
10-1-6: Violations; Penalties
10-1-1: PURPOSES:
The district boundaries and regulations which apply within each of the
districts have been made in accordance with a comprehensive plan designed:
   A.   To promote the health, convenience, order, prosperity, and general
welfare of the citizens of Gooding County, Idaho, that reside in or about the
city of Hagerman.
   B.   To encourage and facilitate the orderly growth and development of the
city.
   C.   To lessen the danger of fire, flood, traffic hazards and other threats
to public welfare.
   D.   To secure economy in the services provided by the city.
   E.   To stabilize and enhance property values, and to facilitate adequate
provision for transportation, water, sewage, schools, and other public
requirements.
   F.   To clarify what is expected of new development in order for it to be in
harmony with existing and future development in the Hagerman area. (Ord. 989,
6-4-1996)
10-1-2: DECLARATION:
In establishing the districts, the boundaries thereof, and the regulations
applying within each of the districts, due and careful consideration was given,
among other things, to the suitability of land for particular uses with a view
to conserving the value of buildings and encouraging the most appropriate use
of land throughout the city and area of impact. (Ord. 989, 6-4-1996)
10-1-3: INTERPRETATION AND INTENT:
It is the intent of the city council that the regulations and restrictions as
set forth in this title shall also be interpreted and construed as to further
the purposes of this title and the objectives and characteristics of the
respective districts. (Ord. 989, 6-4-1996)
10-1-4: ZONING PERMIT:
   A.   Contents Of Application: The application for zoning permit shall be
signed by the owner or applicant attesting to the truth and exactness of all
